Songjiang 76

District Chiefs' Joint Meeting Record The county government convened a joint meeting of district chiefs yesterday to discuss and decide on events: (1) The Finance Bureau was ordered to solicit customs tax and labor cases. Because the county has had poor harvests and the people are in poverty for many years, it is now planned to change the method. The Finance Bureau will issue a receipt and order the rejection of borrowing from various industries to offset it. The two yuan of extra grain tax will be restored to offset it, and all of it will be solved as scheduled. On one side, the county will circulate to all districts and summon the township police to earnestly persuade. (1) The administrative expenses of each district are ordered to be reduced. The district chiefs proposed temporarily and resolved to ask the county government to consider the difficulties of the districts in handling affairs. The new budget will be postponed for implementation and disbursements will still be made according to the old plan.

The First District Plans to Build a New West Baidu Bridge The main roads in the area of the First District Office have been leveled and repaired, and the tributary back street bridges and roads have been repaired for more than one-third. However, the Xiunan Bridge outside the west and the West Baidu are busy with traffic, and the ferryboats at West Baidu are quite inconvenient. Therefore, gentlemen Lei Junyan, Du Shizhou, Wu Chengfu, etc., initiated the construction of a new cement bridge. The district office convened a meeting of all sectors of society. Because the project is huge, it is a pioneering initiative in Songcheng. For the sake of prudence, a bridge construction committee was formed to preside over the handling. It is heard that the project cost is about five or six thousand gold. In addition to the subsidy from the district office, the rest will be undertaken by Lei Jun and others to raise funds.

Fengxian 77

Implementation Methods of the Five-County Joint Defense: The Civil Affairs Department has ordered the five-county joint defense to be implemented. County Magistrate Shen Qingchen of this county has scheduled a meeting for discussion on September 6th, and instructed to first prepare detailed methods for review. Therefore, County Magistrate Shen has already consulted with Jinshan, Nanhui, Shangyu, and Songjiang counties, requesting their attendance at the time. In addition, detailed implementation methods for the joint defense plan will be formulated for compliance. Besides the coastal area, which is vast and difficult to manage, the Songchang Salt Police Bureau and the Suzhou Customs Anti-Smuggling Department will be jointly assisted. For the border areas inland, inspection stations will be established to specialize in investigation. At Zhangjiatang and other places bordering Songjiang, Nanhui, Fengxian, and Shangyu counties, which are particularly important locations, several police officers will be transferred from the public security bureaus of the respective counties to form a joint police station for garrisoning.

Police Team Captures Bandits: Yang Xingsheng, the squad leader of the Second Police Platoon stationed in the village, received a tip-off that bandits led by Xie Youcai and others were planning to rob in partnership at Yanduntou. He ordered plainclothes officers to secretly investigate in Tinglin Town, Songjiang County, a neighboring area, the day before yesterday. They were captured in a certain cigarette shop. However, one of the bandits' accomplices was said to be a water police patrolman, which led to a misunderstanding and almost caused a conflict. The local public security sub-bureau detained both parties together. Yesterday evening, Squad Leader Yang prepared proof to welcome them back for interrogation. According to their confession, they had a meeting at Li Jiasheng's and Xia Laohu's houses in Huan'an, with a total of twenty-four people. They elected Xia Zexian as their leader and each contributed forty-five yuan to purchase Mauser rifles for use. However, they did not directly disclose their actions. "We only know that they will gather in Yanduntou in a few days to kidnap several senior members of a certain butcher shop and a certain flower shop." Several accomplices they confessed have also been successively arrested by Captain Yang this morning, including Gu Meilin. The suspect was previously arrested and released on bail for suspicion in the Zhuanghang arson case. He has now admitted that he went to the home of Dai Xiaocai, a co-criminal who has already been executed, with Tofu Afu at the end of June in the lunar calendar to purchase a Browning pistol. Therefore, Captain Yang has transferred the two bandits to the county for investigation. As for the 53 yuan found on the spot, it is planned to use it to cover the investigation costs of this case, and the rest will be used as reward money.

Changzhou 78

Robbery and Murder Case in the Fifth District: More than ten bandits, each holding a handgun, suddenly came to Zhou Haoda's house in Zhanghaiqiao, Fifth District, Wuyi, on the 30th. After entering the house, the bandit leader demanded a hundred yuan from Haoda, otherwise, "I will take you outside to talk." Haoda refused. The bandit leader twisted him outside and shot him with a handgun, hitting a vital spot, and he fell to the ground and died immediately. Then the bandit leader led the crowd into the house to search and rob, and then left triumphantly. Today (the 2nd), news came that the bandit leader in this case was Jin, who had previously led a crowd to rob and kill people in Tangjia. He has been hiding in Shanghai for a long time and has now sneaked back to commit crimes again. It can be said that he is extremely bold. The victim is afraid of the bandit's power and has not yet reported the case.

It is now decided that the fundraising of remaining customs treasury bonds will be stopped, and the grain will be borrowed. The urban area will be responsible for 30,000 yuan, and the rural area will raise 60,000 yuan. The Chamber of Commerce will be responsible for raising 10,000 yuan, and the silver shops will be responsible for raising 20,000 yuan. The monthly interest rate is 1.2%, and rice is used as a mortgage. Half of the loan will be paid first on the 3rd of this month, and the remaining half will be paid on the 15th.

Wuxi 86

Bandits Rob and Shoot the Victim: Zhang Guoliang, a 54-year-old farmer from Shengdianqiao, Niandou Jiutu, Seventeenth District (Fuan Township), was robbed by seven or eight bandits who spoke in a strong northern accent and each held a handgun. First, one bandit climbed over the wall and entered the house, opened the gate, and let in four or five bandits. Two bandits stood guard outside the gate. After the bandits entered the room, they tied up Zhang's eldest son, Jin Dayong, and then searched wildly, and tied up Zhang Guoliang's wife, and ordered her to keep quiet. At that time, Guoliang secretly took a police gong, climbed onto the roof, and rang the gong for help. The bandits were furious and fired seven or eight shots at Guoliang. He could not dodge in time and was hit by three shots. Blood flowed like a fountain, and he fell on the roof. The bandits searched for half an hour before carrying the stolen goods away. It is estimated that the cash, jewelry, clothes, etc. that were robbed were worth about 60-70 yuan. Yesterday morning, the victim Zhang Guoliang hired a boat with his son to the city to go to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. It was found that the bullets had penetrated the bladder, urethra, and other vital organs, and could not be treated. At about 3:00 pm, Zhang was accompanied back to his hometown.

Urgent Progress in Conscripting Labor to Build Roads: The Construction Bureau of Xiyi County was ordered to carry out conscription of labor to build roads. The original plan was to implement the conscription on April 18, and first build the Xichang Provincial Road. Later, due to the summer farming season, it was postponed until after the autumn harvest. Recently, Yao Dixing, the director of the Construction Bureau, believed that the autumn harvest was approaching, and it was necessary to continue the previous achievements, and to subsidize the Huanhu Avenue project so that it could be completed as soon as possible. He specially planned to build the Xiyi Provincial Road first, and then the Xichang Provincial Road after the Xiyi was completed. However, the Xiyi route has been changed since it was measured and notified by the Highway Bureau. All sections from Xuxiang to Panjiaqiao have been changed to walk along the lake. However, there are continuous mountains and few villages within ten miles along the route. It is feared that difficulties will inevitably arise when conscripting labor in the future. Director Yao submitted a report to County Magistrate Pan yesterday, requesting that it be forwarded to the Construction Department for review and handling.

Strange Fetus Produced by a Rural Woman in the Ninth District: Yan Genbao, a villager in Daoshang Village, Taian Township, Ninth District (Beishang Township), Xiyi County, has always been engaged in farming. His wife, Zhang, is over 40 years old. She became pregnant last winter and has been pregnant ever since. Unexpectedly, Zhang suddenly felt severe pain in her abdomen the day before yesterday. Until yesterday morning, she gave birth to a child. The child looked like a monkey, with hair all over its body, bright eyes, and teeth in its mouth. When Zhang saw this, she couldn't help being shocked. At that time, the residents in the surrounding area went to watch and were all amazed. Yan Genbao believed that his wife had given birth to this monster, which he considered ominous, and immediately buried the monster alive in the field in the afternoon of the same day.

Jiaxing 90

Reasons for the Resignation of the Members of the Chamber of Commerce Consolidated Organization Committee: The members of the Jiaxing County Merchant Unified Organization Committee had just taken the oath of office on August 25 and took over the County Chamber of Commerce and the County Merchants Association to work hard. The Wheel Bureau Requests Exemption from Education Fees: The Jiaxing County Education Property Association had previously resolved to collect an education fee of one point per ticket for each small wheel passenger ticket on the inner river to help fund elementary schools, and it has been approved by the Provincial Department to collect fees on a regular basis. The association had also convened the managers of the wheel bureaus to discuss the date of collection and the method of payment. However, few people attended, and the matter has not been resolved. It is now learned that the Education Property Association does not pursue or reorganize the original eroded properties, but only seeks to exploit the people's difficulties. Recently, it has decided to add two cents per tael/stone to the land tax subsidy for this year (this case has been implemented), and also add a certain amount to the slaughter tax. It also wants to add fees to commercial wheel passenger tickets. This is really ignoring the people's difficulties, and the fee collection regulations are also inconsistent. Therefore, the wheel bureaus jointly submitted a request to the provincial and county authorities on the 2nd, ordering the Education Property Association to stop the collection and revoke the original plan in order to comply with laws and regulations.

Jiading 91

Strange Murder Case Discovered in Anting: Fu Pinhua of Wangjiacun, Liuhe, Taicang County, took his wife, Wang, from Shanghai to Anting by car the month before last, intending to take a wheel back to the village. They temporarily stayed in a small teahouse next to the station. Lu Jinzhang, a station worker, and others teased his wife. Her husband, Fu Pinhua, argued with them and was beaten as a result, and then disappeared. Later, it is not known what happened. Stationmaster Zhou Xichen detained Fu Wang and Zhou Peirong and Qiao A'er from the village and handed them over to the local security chief, who forwarded them to the district office and then to the county government, accusing Zhou et al. of forcing marriage without success and requesting an investigation. Chen Chengshen asked about the truth of the matter. Zhou confessed that the woman had fled to his house and there was no forced marriage. The woman also only confessed that she had been teased and that the couple had been beaten. The next day, the county government received a report from the Anting District Office that an unidentified male corpse was found in Chenjiabang in the southeast of the station. Trial Officer Zhang took Fu Wang to inspect the corpse and confirmed that the deceased was indeed her husband. Before his death, his chest and waist were fatally drowned. The suspect Lu Jinzhang was detained for interrogation. County Magistrate Chen believed that the stationmaster Zhou Xichen had fabricated the facts to exonerate the perpetrators and that it was necessary to summon him. He specially sent Zhu, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, to Shanghai on the 29th to contact the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Administration on everything. It is also heard that there have been multiple murder cases within this year in the Kunshan and Jiading counties near the station.

Detectives Search and Assault: Xu A'liu, a boatman, stole 220 bags of rough indica rice from the Shanghai Taikang Rice Shop that the shop had consigned for transport, and had the shop's employee Dai A'san grind them at the Xinsheng Rice Mill in Lujiabang, Qia Xinghe Rice Shop in Huangdu Town in the county. After the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau learned of this, it detained Dai A'san and sent detectives Su Sheng et al. to Jia for extradition with Dai A'san et al. County Magistrate Chen ordered Deng Jinglie, the police squad leader stationed in the town, to assist and detained Jiang Boqing, an employee of Qia Taihe Shop, and sent him to the county. At the same time, according to a report from the district office in the area, the detectives Su Sheng et al. broke into the Gongxing Commercial Firm in the town and searched it for no reason, and beat Tang Dekui, the shop's storekeeper. After learning the situation, County Magistrate Chen ordered Deng, the police squad leader, to investigate and verify the matter.

Refugees Pass Through - One False and One True: On the 28th of last month, Zhang Yuehao, who claimed to be a representative of refugees from Xianning County, Jiangxi, arrived in Anting Town, Eighth District, and asked the town's security corps to issue travel expenses, and his desires were very extravagant. The corps asked where the refugees were, and he replied that they were in Gaochang Temple, Shanghai. The district corps leader suspected that he was impersonating and planned to punish him according to the county order. Zhang saw that he had been exposed and escaped. Yesterday (1st), more than 370 refugees from Xinhua, Hunan, entered the country from Taicang and requested accommodation for one night. The corps agreed and directed them to Bodhi Temple as a place to stay. The next day, they gave them travel expenses and escorted them out of the country in accordance with the regulations.

Ningbo 92

Resolution of the Meat Industry Dispute: The Municipal Government convened representatives of domestic merchants at 10:00 am yesterday (30th) to discuss ways to resolve the slaughtering problem. Special Commissioners Shen Zhennan and Xia Jinxiong from the Provincial Government attended the meeting. Mayor Yang chaired the meeting. As a result, it was decided to set up a temporary slaughterhouse in the east gate, west gate, south gate of the Yangtze River, respectively. From September 1 to October 9, all the restrictions will be lifted when the period expires, and the slaughtering time and the area for the sale of white meat will be stipulated. The long-delayed meat industry turmoil has been completely resolved at this point.

Municipal Government's Handling of the Housing Donation Dispute: The Village and Neighborhood Committees of this city, because the housing donation investigators of the Municipal Government arbitrarily increased housing donations and used police threats, organized a committee to eliminate housing donation disputes and reported it to the Municipal Government for filing. The Municipal Government issued a special order to the Village Committees regarding this case yesterday, stating that the Municipal Government learned from the reports of the Village and Neighborhood Committees that the investigators had arbitrarily estimated the value of the properties in the previous investigation of housing donations, and the Municipal Government deeply regrets this. In order to eliminate this dispute, all the places where the investigators arbitrarily estimated the value in the previous investigation should be investigated and reported, and staff will be sent to investigate and handle the matter fairly. In addition, if the investigators have any intimidating or fraudulent behavior outside, the committee should report the facts to the government at any time for investigation and punishment.

Correspondence 93

Shanghai County Public Security Bureau Letter 94

Regarding the matter of your esteemed newspaper carrying a report today stating that on the morning of the 1st, four automobiles came from Shanghai to Zhuanqiao, carrying about thirty bandits with twenty Mauser pistols, intending to loot. The report further stated that the defense corps went to suppress them and seized four Mauser pistols. After reading this, we were extremely surprised. Zhuanqiao is under the jurisdiction of the First Police Station of our Bureau's Second Branch. The station also has assigned police officers. This morning, we received a report from Li Weimin, an officer of the Second Branch, stating that more than thirty soldiers and police officers dispatched by the Songjiang Joint Defense Command arrived at the bridge at various times in the afternoon, claiming to be under orders to intercept deserters. They requested the assistance of the police officers stationed at the station and jointly inspected passing automobiles and pedestrians. They found nothing until evening, and the soldiers and police officers returned to Songjiang. There was no discovery of bandits or seizure of Mauser pistols. Today, our Bureau again sent personnel for a detailed investigation. According to Mr. Ma, a staff member of Zhuanqiao Station, and the head of the police station, no bandits were found yesterday, and no Mauser pistols were seized. As this matter concerns local security, we are making a factual statement and request that it be corrected in the newspaper. Shanghai County Public Security Bureau. September 2nd.

Important Educational News

Overseas Chinese Elementary School Established in Osaka 95

(Osaka Correspondence) Chinese have resided in Osaka for more than eighty years, with a population reaching over five thousand. All children of overseas Chinese have been studying in Japanese schools because there is no overseas Chinese elementary school. Consequently, they receive foreign education and hardly know themselves as Chinese. They speak Japanese and their behavior tends towards Japanese. This certainly poses the danger of national assimilation. Several years ago, prominent overseas Chinese in Osaka suggested establishing a Chinese school, but due to improper management, it was repeatedly started and stopped. Currently, Li Ziyu and Chai Zijing, hired from Tsinghua University in Peiping, are responsible for preparatory matters. All procedures have been properly arranged, the school has been registered with the Ministry of Education, and permission has been obtained from the Japanese authorities. Regarding funding, the Beibang Guild will provide an annual subsidy of 4,000 Japanese yen. Tuition will be waived for students. The school will be divided into higher and lower elementary levels and is scheduled to open on September 1st.

Ministry of Education Clarifies Doubts Regarding Membership and Executive Committee of Educational Associations 97

The Ministry of Education, based on a report from the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education and a request from the Qu County Government for clarification on membership and the term of office of executive committee members in educational associations, specifically instructed the Zhejiang Department of Education to clarify: The acquisition of membership in an educational association should be based on the formal announcement of the membership qualification review committee. According to Article 24 of the Educational Association Regulations, city and county educational associations hold elections once a year. Also, according to Article 20 of the regulations, a membership qualification review committee is to be organized two months before each election. If the Qu County Educational Association has not reached the election period, it cannot organize a qualification review committee to solicit current school staff who have not joined the association as members. As for the term of office of executive committee members, it should comply with the provisions of Article 24 of the regulations, with an election held every year. Please be informed and instructed to comply accordingly.

Yuan Jiapu, a member of the Shandong Provincial Government, and He Siyuan, of the Education Department, recently telegraphed the Examination Yuan and the Ministry of Education, stating that yesterday, after being proposed by Jiapu and Siyuan and decided by the Shandong Provincial Government meeting, the principal and interest of more than 275,700 yuan owed by the Shandong Donggang Public Office to the province, and the 100,000 yuan of share exchange certificates from the China Industrial Bank, plus the annual official interest of 6,000 yuan, will be used as the Shandong Provincial Library Committee fund. This is truly good news for the Shandong library fund.

Recent Educational News from Anhui Province 102

The Department of Education Oversees Enrollment for Provincial High Schools: The Anhui Department of Education, because the principals of provincial high schools had not yet been announced but enrollment was urgent, specially appointed Supervisor Wang Dexi to oversee high schools and Wei Congxu, director of elementary school management, to oversee enrollment for high schools and affiliated elementary schools. Section chiefs Li Zhongxiang, Zhang Xinpei, and Chen Xifang, supervisors Wu Liangfu, Wang Dexi, and Ye Minghui, and translation director Pan Chuji were appointed to organize an examination committee to set questions and supervise the exams. Apart from the affiliated elementary school's new student exams, which were held on the 21st of this month, the high school new student exams were completed on the 25th and 26th, with oral exams held on the 27th. Security was tight and extremely serious. Once the scores of each subject's exam papers have been graded, the results will be announced.

Provincial Popular Education Center Renamed Public Education Center: The Department of Education, based on the Improvement Plan for Social Education resolved at the Second National Education Conference, with the Public Education Center as the implementing agency for social education, and with Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces having already renamed their old Popular Education Centers as Public Education Centers to achieve uniformity, has decided to rename the province's Provincial First, Second, and Third Popular Education Centers as the First, Second, and Third Public Education Centers.

Cessation of Funding for Luyang Lakeside Middle School: Private Luyang Lakeside Middle School is poorly managed. Based on the inspection report by former Supervisor Cheng Zongchao in May of the 18th year, the Department of Education found that students' levels were elementary, teachers' teaching methods were inadequate, and after six years of establishment, there was no achievement. The Hefei County Magistrate was ordered to inform the school's board of directors to promptly find a way to rectify the school based on the rural environment. In May of this year, Supervisor Li Guanglie inspected the school again and reported that no one was responsible for school affairs, the administrative organization was unsound, the implementation of discipline was not standardized, the teaching staff was largely unqualified, and the content was extremely corrupt. The Department of Education, considering that the school had not complied with orders, ignored education, and failed to be punished, losing the fundamental purpose of rectifying private schools, specifically, according to Article 8 of the Temporary Regulations on Subsidies for Private Secondary Schools in Anhui Province, has decided to cease the school's subsidy from the 19th year.

First Day of Literacy Campaign in Shanghai County 104

The literacy campaign is the foundational work for popularizing education. Literacy is the tool for acquiring knowledge, just as musical notation is for music. Without knowing musical notation, one cannot distinguish the length and pitch of sounds. The inability to popularize education in China stems from this. According to recent statistics, illiteracy accounts for 60% in cities and over 90% in rural areas. On average, over 80% of the national population has not received education. In such a situation, how can our economy and culture compare with those of the world's major powers? Therefore, the Central Government has listed the literacy campaign as the top priority among the seven major movements, which is evident. Although Shanghai County is close to the city, its jurisdiction is mostly rural, with numerous farmers, so the literacy campaign is particularly important. Currently, the County Party Headquarters, together with the County Government, will hold large-scale literacy campaign promotion meetings in various districts starting from September 1st. Yesterday was the first day, and representatives from the two agencies, carrying slogans, leaflets, and booklets, went to the First District (i.e., Minhang), where a meeting was held at the public sports ground. Groups from agriculture, commerce, and education attended. District Chief Wu Jingqing presided. After the formalities, the meeting commenced. First, the chairman reported, followed by speeches from Fu Dianying, representative of the County Government, Jiang Yanqiu, representative of the County Party Headquarters, and Jin Zuobin from the Public Education Center. The meeting adjourned around 3:00 PM, and a parade was held around the area.

Chen Zuping Goes to the United States to Study Municipal Administration 105

Mr. Chen Zuping, courtesy name Hengfu, is from Wuxing, Zhejiang, and is the eldest son of Chen Aishi, the current Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Finance Department. Mr. Chen graduated from Guanghua University with a Bachelor of Arts degree and has served as a follower secretary to the National Government Committee. Recently, he went to the United States at his own expense to study municipal administration in the graduate school of the University of Michigan. When he returns to China, he will travel through Europe to inspect municipal administration in various countries for reference.

Opening of Night School and Correspondence Course in Chinese Language 106

Mr. Zou Dengtai is learned and erudite, well-versed in Chinese culture. He has served as a professor of Chinese studies at Shanghai National Jiaotong University, National Business College, private Southern University, Cang Sheng University, and Datong University. He has also authored "Comprehensive Compilations of the Five Classics," "Stepping Stones to History," "Stepping Stones to Writing," "Original Theories of Literary Styles," and "Detailed Commentary on the Shuowen Jiezi." He is a figure of prominence in Chinese studies. To preserve Chinese culture, he has established a Chinese language night school at Jinye School on Baike Road and the Dyeing Industry School on Jiangyin Street outside the west gate, and he is also offering a correspondence course, providing earnest guidance and teaching with great enthusiasm. As a result, there is a continuous stream of students seeking admission. As the fall semester begins, a prosperous situation for his students can be imagined.

Hong Kong Chinese Football Team 113

Welcomed by Hu Wenhu After Arriving in Singapore

(Singapore Correspondence, August 20th) The Chinese football team, also known as the Tiger Team, arrived from Hong Kong on the Dadehao ship on the 12th of this month. After 9:00 AM today, Pier 6/7 of Tanjong Pagar suddenly became lively. Representatives from the Singapore Chinese Sports Association and the Chinese Football Association, as well as reporters from various newspapers, gathered to welcome them. Mr. Hu Wenhu specially sent his representative, Mr. Hu Guigeng, and several cars to greet them. At 10:30 AM, the ship finally docked, and the welcomers boarded the ship, shaking hands with each player as a greeting. Soon after, they disembarked and boarded Hu Wenhu's specially prepared cars, heading to the villa in Pasir Panjang for a stay. While on the ship, the reporter took the opportunity to interview Mr. Ye Jiugao, the team's leader. His important remarks are recorded below: "Question: How many people are in your team this time?" Mr. Ye replied, "There are twenty of us in total. Besides me, there are Chen Yuehua (deputy leader and secretary), Yao Muqiu (advisor), Jiang Fuxing (treasurer), Ou Jiesheng (trainer), Li Yuku (captain), Chen Xipei (vice-captain), Wu Jinquan, Sun Jinshun, Huang Baisong, Liang Yutang, He Zuoxian, Huang Ruihua, Luo Weimin, Huang Bing, He Jiaqiang, Li Hongbei, Liang Kuirong, Mai Guodong, Shi Peitian, and Li Guozhao (all players) and Mrs. Sun Jinshun." "Question: Why didn't your team participate in the Chinese expedition team's expedition to Europe and America?" "Answer: When that team was initiated, it did not obtain the consent of our association." "Question: Will Cao Guicheng and Chen Guangyao participate in your team in the battles in Southeast Asia?" "Answer: We will invite Mr. Cao and Mr. Chen to participate when the time comes." "Question: Is it your association that controls Cao Guicheng and Chen Guangyao's participation in the expedition team?" "Answer: This is a personal action. Our association takes a non-interference attitude towards any member's participation." "Question: How many places will you go to this trip?" "Answer: It has not been decided yet." "Question: Did you fight in Annam? What were the results?" "Answer: Our team played three matches in Annam, winning twice and drawing once. The first time was against the local champion team, winning four to one. The second time was against the All-Star team, winning four to one. The last time was against the All-Star team again, drawing two to two." Also, Mr. Hu Wenhu, owner of the Yong An Tang in this city, is the honorary president of the association. Before the team came south, they had already telegraphed Mr. Hu to inform him of the travel schedule. They also repeatedly telegraphed when the ship was approaching the Singapore Strait. Therefore, after the team disembarked, Mr. Hu ordered people to welcome them and reside in the villa in Pasir Panjang. It is reported that Mr. Hu has scheduled to host a banquet for the team at the Viroki Club at 7:00 PM today and has invited reporters from various newspapers to attend. When the time comes, with wine and lights, it will surely be a lively scene.

Local News

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Old and New 117

The General Manager Prepares to Hand Over Duties 118

New Developments in Negotiations with the San Teh Tang

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company’s General Manager, Tze Chen Hsi-tseng, has been permitted to resign after personally submitting his resignation. Li Chung-kung’s succession marks the end of a phase. Li has already travelled from Shanghai to Beijing to discuss reorganizing the bureau’s affairs, as well as the most critical financial issues, with Minister of Communications Wang Po-chun. He is expected to arrive in Shanghai within the next day or two to take over. The acting General Manager, Tsai Tzu-ping, is preparing to hand over duties. Amidst this transition, our reporter paid a special visit to Mr. Tsai yesterday. The various issues are recorded below:

Acting General Manager Tsai's Parting Words on Taking Over 119

Initially, my intention was to temporarily manage for ten days, but due to the San Teh Tang case, I came to the bureau twice and have now been in charge for exactly one month. During this period, Mr. Tsai discussed matters with the heads of various departments but did not have a face-to-face meeting with all the bureau's staff. Now that the new appointment has been decided and the handover is imminent, he gathered all the staff for a farewell speech at noon one day. Mr. Tsai's speech was divided into three parts: (1) He explained the course of his temporary assignment, from ten days to one month. (2) He expressed his gratitude for the dedication and support of all the staff during this month. (3) He stated that military transportation was very important during this month. After his arrival, he did not cause any delays in military transportation and also took care of business operations, ensuring that no ships were idle and maintaining the regular schedules of various routes. Regarding business operations, the internal coordination of Section Chief Shen Chung-yi and the external efforts and guidance of Deputy Section Chief Li Yun-liang were particularly effective. He deeply relied on their assistance in managing the overall situation.

Mr. Li to Assume Office Immediately. Mr. Tsai Told the Reporter, 120

I have already met with Deputy Minister Li. Now Li has entered Beijing, probably to discuss various reorganization matters with Minister Wang. General Manager Li is expected to arrive in Shanghai this Thursday (i.e., the 4th) to assume office, or he may arrive at the bureau. Even if there is a slight delay in Beijing, he can decide to assume office by the 5th at the latest. I (Mr. Tsai refers to himself) will immediately hand over duties and go to Beijing after Deputy Minister Li arrives at the bureau. I will not stay in Shanghai.

Raising Back Pay for Staff. The Bureau Is Riddled with Problems. 121

The most difficult issue is finance. Mr. Tsai's term coincided with internal and external communication challenges. The salaries of the bureau's employees have been in arrears for two months. Considering the difficulties faced by the staff, Mr. Tsai has raised a sum of money. He has already notified the staff yesterday that, no matter what, he will manage to issue one month's salary to provide for their livelihood before he leaves office. According to Mr. Tsai's statement to the reporter yesterday, the payment should be made today or tomorrow. Mr. Tsai has stated that he will not accept his own salary of one thousand yuan for serving as acting general manager for this month. He is willing to fulfill his obligations and only accept reimbursement for travel expenses to and from Beijing and Shanghai.

Progress on Wharf Negotiations. The Kin Li Yuen Wharf Negotiations 122

are the most important matter during Mr. Tsai's term. Since the bureau sent Kao Shuo to negotiate with the San Teh Tang's arbitrators, the French side has created numerous obstacles, preventing the matter from being resolved quickly. Yesterday, Mr. Tsai told the reporter that our arbitrators recently discussed the matter with the San Teh Tang's representatives, and there has been new progress on the whole. The San Teh Tang has agreed to continue leasing the Kin Li Yuen wharf to the bureau for management, but it still insists on taking back the Kin Li Yuen's warehouse and has indicated that it will not lease it out again. Because the wharf is no longer a problem, our side is now raising new issues regarding the warehouse. Since they do not want to lease it, we propose to buy the warehouse to prevent the excellent warehouse from being damaged. This is currently in progress. In general, the purchase of the warehouse needs to be vigorously pursued after the new General Manager takes over, to achieve the goal of having the wharves and warehouses managed by the bureau. Another piece of news is that Father Hsia Hsi of the French San Teh Tang is currently seeking instructions from the Paris General Cathedral, and has not yet received a reply, so the negotiations have temporarily stopped.

Bureau Staff Resignations. After the Death of Chao Tieh-chiao, Hung 123

Yen-pin resigned as head of the Accounting Department, and Wang Tzu-chien also resigned as head of the General Affairs Department. Because Mr. Tsai did not bring anyone to the bureau, he temporarily appointed bureau staff to act as heads. In addition, Lung Hsia-chu, head of the Shipping Department, also tendered his resignation. Mr. Tsai tried to persuade him to stay, but to no avail, so he appointed Shen Chi-yun, a staff member of the Shipping Section, as temporary head. The vacant positions of the department heads will be filled after the new appointee arrives.

Recent Status of River and Sea Merchant Ships. Six Yangtze River ships had already 124

resumed their regular schedules, but now they have suspended service again due to an incident. It was learned yesterday that the upper reaches vessel, the Omei, has been released and will be put back into service after repairs. The Chiang Ching, which was damaged by collisions with the Ta Ta and Ta Chi, will soon be repaired and resume service. One ship each remains in service on the northern and southern oceans.

The Remittance of Indemnities and Loans for August Has Been Made. 125

Greatly Valued by Foreign Newspapers.

The Shanghai Times reported that, with the slight recovery in silver prices last week, the Customs saved no less than 100,000 taels on the foreign payments due in August. As the end of the month fell on a Sunday, all indemnity payments and domestic and foreign debt payments were made by the Finance Department on August 30, totaling 3,870,237.29 taels. At a time when world trade is sluggish and all countries are affected, China's customs revenue can fulfill all guaranteed domestic and foreign debts with a surplus, which is quite noteworthy.

to Visit His Mother.

Ke Ching-en, the mayor of Qingdao, along with his wife, sons and daughters (five in total), and three servants, traveled south from Qingdao on the Japanese ship "Tientsin Maru" on the morning of the 1st. They arrived in Shanghai at around 3 PM yesterday. The ship docked at the Huangpu Wharf. Also arriving were Lu Chuan, the Director of the Finance Bureau, and Cheng Chao-ching, the Director of the Port Affairs Bureau. Those who came to welcome them included Xu Hsiao-chai, the captain of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau's Water Patrol Team, and several detectives, who were there to provide assistance. According to Mr. Ke, the new mayor, Hu Hsin, was traveling to Qingdao on the Zhenhai warship. When the Tientsin Maru left Qingdao at 8 AM, the warship had not yet arrived, so they did not meet. Because his mother is ill and he needs to return to Hangzhou to visit her, and also because he is feeling slightly unwell, he did not linger in Shanghai and took the Shanghai-Hangzhou express train back to Hangzhou at around 5 PM. The date of his trip to Beijing has not yet been decided, but he will have to go to Beijing eventually. At that time, Mr. Ke was taking care of the luggage and sending people to buy Shanghai-Hangzhou train tickets, and seemed quite hurried.

The Order Lifting the Ban on Flour Exports Has Not Arrived. 131

Flour Mills Reduce Working Hours.

Although there is talk of lifting the ban on the export of flour to the north, the Customs has not yet received an official document from the Ministry of Finance for several days. Therefore, the export of flour to Tianjin is still subject to the ban, which has had a significant impact on the flour merchants in the port, due to sluggish sales. It was reported that some flour mills have reduced their working hours, starting the day before yesterday, by about 40% compared to normal, in order to avoid stockpiling. On the other hand, they are still making every effort to urge the National Government to lift the ban as soon as possible to alleviate the merchants' difficulties, but it is not known whether they will be able to obtain approval.

British Naval Escorts for Jardine Matheson and Butterfield & Swire Ships on the Yangtze River. Recently, due to frequent attacks in the Wuxue area of the upper Yangtze River, the various ships have requested the British military in Hankou to dispatch a platoon of soldiers to be stationed on the ships for the safety of passengers and cargo, starting from September 1st. Shanghai-Hankou Remittances Are Being Collected and Remitted as Usual. 135

The Shanghai Silk Weavers Association stated that many of its members trade with merchants from Changsha. Since the central army recovered Changsha, the overall situation in the city has been stable. However, the merchants from Changsha stationed in Shanghai to purchase goods still have some excuses regarding the remittance of funds. As the end of the eighth month approaches and financial turnover is crucial, the association was planning to write to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to inquire with the Changsha Chamber of Commerce. However, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent a letter yesterday stating that it had received an urgent telegram from the Changsha Chamber of Commerce stating that, due to rumors in the provincial capital, financial activities had been temporarily suspended. However, the market is now peaceful as usual, and Shanghai-Hankou remittances are being collected and remitted as usual. They hope that this information will be passed on to the various merchant guilds. Accordingly, they have recorded the telegram and notified them for their information. It is reported that the association has sent letters to its members to inform them.

An Appeal Regarding the Disaster in Yunmeng Caused by the Communists. 136

The Hubei Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation Asks for Funds for Relief.

The Hubei Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation telegraphed that it had received an urgent telegram from the entire executive and supervisory committee of the Yunmeng County Chamber of Commerce, leading hundreds of refugees, stating that on the morning of the 6th of this month, thousands of communists suddenly occupied the city, killing, looting, and ravaging it. They only left by their original route at 2 PM on the 9th, after seeing planes dropping bombs. The period of occupation lasted four days, and the disasters that occurred were too horrible to describe. On the second day, they forced the merchants and residents to pay 70,000 yuan. After the money was paid on the following day, they ransacked the cloth merchants, causing a total loss of over 40,000 bolts of white cloth and over ten bales of foreign yarn. About ten large and small grocery stores, about ten large and small piece goods stores, and about ten herbal medicine stores were all looted. The number of small merchants and residents engaged in flower, grain, handicraft, and cooked food businesses who were displaced is countless. In addition, over twenty hostages were taken from the white cloth, piece goods, and grocery businesses, and over thirty residents were asked to pay ransom ranging from one thousand to ten thousand yuan. So far, no one has been able to redeem them. Furthermore, the bandits brutally killed six people when they left, and the rest has not yet been verified. In total, the losses of merchants and residents account for more than half of their assets. Since the county was established hundreds of years ago, there has never been such a catastrophe. The successive county magistrates have been collecting gun money from the merchants, amounting to thousands of yuan, but they have not seen a single new gun purchased. In times of crisis, they only run away with their guns, leaving ten out of ten homes empty, with wives crying and children weeping, staging this tragic scene. The association has convened a joint meeting of refugees and merchants, and resolved that, in addition to the association organizing a fundraising group to freely solicit donations from major cities and philanthropists for relief, they are telegraphing to express their hot zeal for relief, and to quickly forward the telegram to the Hubei Provincial Government and the Hubei Department of Civil Affairs, pleading for compassion.

Page 14

Give subsidies for disaster relief, to help the urgent needs. Considering that the county is small and the people are economical, they suddenly encountered a major change. The appeal could not be delayed. The situation is truly pitiful. In accordance with the previous telegram, we respectfully request people in Shanghai or Hubei merchants to make donations to help the surviving people after the catastrophe. We will be eternally grateful. [Signed] Su Tai-yu, Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation.

Negotiations on the "New Canton" Ship Case. 137

It is Necessary to Ensure That the Case Is Handled and Investigated.

In the case of the "New Canton" ship being sunk by the Japanese ship "Tatsuno Maru," the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company filed a lawsuit in the Shanghai Provisional Court in accordance with the International Maritime Law. However, the Shanghai branch of the Nippon Yusen Kaisha stated that the "Tatsuno Maru" was not at fault in the collision, and if the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company had any demands on the company, it should file a lawsuit in the Japanese court in accordance with formal litigation procedures. The Ministry of Communications believes that the Japanese side is not acknowledging responsibility, so it has sent a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, asking it to promptly notify the Japanese side to handle the case so that it can be resolved as soon as possible.

Recent News on the Port Affairs Bureau's Purchase of the Ta Ta Wharf. 138

A Solution Is Expected Soon.

Since the Shanghai Municipal Port Affairs Bureau began negotiating with the various shipping companies for the purchase of the Ta Ta Wharf at the 16th Pier in the South City, the bureau has prepared funds to buy back the wharves of companies such as the Min Hsing, which have already returned to the bureau's ownership. However, the Ta Ta Wharf has not yet been resolved because the purchase price is higher than that of other wharves, amounting to 100,000 yuan. Before Mayor Chang left Shanghai, he promised that the municipal government would provide cash to purchase the wharf. Later, when the mayor left Shanghai due to an incident, the municipal government agreed to pay 20,000 yuan per year for five years. Upon hearing this, the company had no intention of temporarily transferring ownership. It is now heard that there is a solution being discussed, with the result being 60% cash and 40% municipal bonds. If so, a formal resolution is expected soon.

The Lawyers Association of the Republic of China has initiated the expansion of the International Lawyers Association to promote the spirit of Chinese legislation and to unify the legislative principles of individualistic and communistic countries with the legislative principles of the Three Principles of the People. The association has recently received several letters from the Chinese Embassy in Sweden and the consulates in Penang, etc., all stating that they admire the association's efforts to improve the legal system for the purpose of a better life for mankind. In addition to forwarding the entrusted items to a certain lawyers' association, they have also attached the name and address of the association for reference. It is learned that Mr. Fukushima, a Japanese national, had previously lobbied in Europe and the United States for this purpose but was unsuccessful. Now that Chinese ambassadors and consuls abroad are happily supporting the National Lawyers Association's continued organizational efforts, it should be able to achieve its goal and open a new era of rule of law for the world.

The Red Cross' Committee to Amend the Articles of Association. 140

Fourth Meeting.

The Committee to Amend the Articles of Association of the Chinese Red Cross held its fourth meeting at 2 PM on September 1st. The attendees included Li Chen-pang, Hung Yen-pin, Yeh Chih-sheng, Wang Pei-yuan, Liu Hong-sheng, Hsu Hsi-chun, Hsueh Shao-ting, Yang Ke, Chiang Ta-chiu, and Wu Chia-san. Chairman Wen Lan-ting was on leave, so Wang Pei-yuan served as chairman. After performing the ceremony and reading the minutes of the previous meeting, which were approved without any objections, the chairman signed them. (1) The chairman read the reply from the Standing Committee, entrusting the committee to draft the rules of procedure for the election of standing members and various supplementary rules, and asked for a public decision. It was decided that the committee would draft the rules and inform the Standing Committee. (2) The chairman proposed that, having agreed to draft the rules for the Standing Committee, drafters should be appointed. Hung Yen-pin was elected as the drafter for the Standing Member Election Law, and Yeh Chih-sheng was elected as the drafter for the Rules of Procedure. (3) Yeh Chih-sheng proposed that the Articles of Association of the Chinese Red Cross be submitted for a second reading, which was approved. The articles were then discussed one by one. Yeh Chih-sheng stated that Article 1, "The association is a legal corporation in law," should be changed to "an international charitable organization." Hung Yen-pin stated that in Article 2, the word "佛" (Buddha) in the "日內瓦佛條約" (Geneva Buddha Treaty) should be changed to "弗" (not) according to its transliteration and that English name should be added in parentheses. He also stated that Article 4 should be moved to the last article of the articles of association. Hsueh Shao-ting stated that the "棺柩所" (coffin place) in Article 7 should be changed to "施材所" (material distribution place). Hung Yen-pin stated that the phrase "以上列各機關之規則另定之" (The rules for the above-mentioned agencies shall be determined separately) in Article 1 can be deleted and moved to the end of Article 7. Wang Pei-yuan stated that the phrase "器械藥品綳帶等" (instruments, medicines, bandages, etc.) in Article 9, paragraph 1, was unclear. Hung Yen-pin stated that this article should be changed to "藥品綳帶等治療用之器械及消耗品" (medicines, bandages, and other instruments and consumables for treatment). Chiang Ta-chiu stated that Chapter 3, "Organization," and Chapter 4, "Affairs," should be changed to Chapter 3, "Affairs," and Chapter 4, "Organization," in accordance with the old articles of association. Yang Ke seconded. Yeh Chih-sheng stated that Articles 14, 15, and 16 in Chapter 3 should be moved after Article 61 in Chapter 9, and Article 17 should be moved after Article 46 in Chapter 5. Hung Yen-pin stated that "代表大會" (Congress of Representatives) should be changed to "會員大會" (General Meeting of Members). Also, the phrase "主席辦理會務、代表本會監督、及任免所有職員" (The chairman shall handle the affairs of the association, represent the association in supervision, and appoint and remove all staff) in Article 31 should be changed to "主席辦理會務、代表本會及監督與任免所有職員" (The chairman shall handle the affairs of the association, represent the association and supervise, and appoint and remove all staff). Wang Pei-yuan stated that in Chapter 5, "Property," a clause should be added stating that "all assets of the association shall be reported to the National Government for record-keeping, and all assets of the branches shall be reported to the general association for record-keeping by the general association." Hung Yen-pin stated that the phrase "大會之主席、由常議會議長充之" (The chairman of the congress shall be the chairman of the standing committee) in Article 38 is too limited in number. Yeh Chih-sheng seconded, and it was changed to "大會之主席、由常議會正副議長及執行委員會正副主席充之" (The chairman of the congress shall be the chairman and vice-chairman of the standing committee and the chairman and vice-chairman of the executive committee). Chiang Ta-chiu stated that Article 59 should be moved after Article 30. Yang Ke stated that Chapter 9, "Rewards and Punishments," should be divided into two chapters, and the word "punishments" is also inappropriate and should be changed to Chapter 9, "Rewards," and Chapter 10, "Discipline." Yeh Chih-sheng stated that the original word "三" (three) in Chapter 10 should be deleted. Chiang Ta-chiu stated that the change of "Congress of Representatives" to "General Meeting of Members" and Article 62 still need to be studied. The chairman stated that they will be discussed again during the third reading. The meeting adjourned after 5 PM.

The Kiangsu and Chekiang Silk Weaving Associations Petition for Amendment of the Factory Law. 141

The Kiangsu and Chekiang Silk Weaving Associations telegraphed Minister Kung of the Ministry of Industry, Commerce and Labor of the National Government in the capital again, requesting an amendment to the Factory Law. The original telegram stated that, after receiving the ministry's approval number 1494, it was submitted to a joint conference of the two provinces for discussion. Everyone believed that China's production is backward, and its industry is still in its infancy. Most factories are small-scale operations, barely enough to make a living, and do not have the financial resources for such large-scale equipment. It is the general opinion of the association that the complete and perfect nature of this law is beneficial to industry and commerce, but it does not apply to China's factories in their current state. The delegates of the silk industry of Kiangsu and Chekiang provinces, at an extraordinary joint meeting, have decided to re-petition for an amendment to Article 1 of the Factory Law, which states that "this law applies to factories that use steam, electricity, or water power to operate machinery and regularly employ 'thirty or more' workers." It should be amended to "(... three thousand...)". They should therefore telegraph to clear the ears and to respectfully ask the ministry to verify and approve the petition to the Executive Yuan to consult the Legislative Yuan to amend the law in order to protect industry and maintain commerce, and must not be in a panic and specially ordered to arrive.

The Yung An Cotton Mill Rice Subsidy Dispute Resolved. 142

The Union's Request for Rice Subsidies Rejected.

Maintaining the Mill's Fair Price Policy.

The Yung An Textile Factory No. 2 Union requested a rice subsidy, which resulted in a dispute. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs convened a mediation meeting, but no agreement was reached. The labor side then submitted a petition to the Municipal Government for arbitration. It is now heard that the labor-management arbitration committee of the municipal government has ruled on the matter, with the main points being: (1) The union's request for a rice subsidy should be rejected. (2) The mill's fair price policy should be maintained. This policy shall be suspended only when the price of rice falls below 13 yuan. The full text of the reasoning is as follows: "The price of rice in this city has been high for several months. The Yung An Textile Factory No. 2 Union believes that the wages of the workers are meager and their livelihood is difficult. They requested that the capital side provide a rice subsidy. The mediation committee held a meeting, but the capital side insisted that there was no precedent for rice subsidies in Chinese cotton mills and could not agree. As a result, the mediation failed. The committee then convened an arbitration meeting. The representatives of the capital side submitted a statement, still claiming that they were experiencing business difficulties and could not afford to grant the union's request for a rice subsidy. The statement went on to say that in 1926, due to high rice prices, the mill adopted a policy of selling rice at a fair price in the factory, and this has been implemented again, with a sales point set up, and this has been in operation for almost a month to provide assistance. The committee then inquired in detail about the mill's fair price policy. According to the representatives of the capital side, the mill's fair price policy was decided by the board of directors and started on August 1st. The purchase price of the white rice was 18 yuan per picul, and the fair price was 13 yuan per picul. Workers who have worked in the factory for four days or more will receive a fair price rice coupon for one yuan each. Workers who have worked in the factory for nine days or more will receive two fair price rice coupons. Workers who work in the factory can buy four yuan worth of fair-priced rice per month. The mill sells an average of 50 piculs of fair-priced rice per day, which means that the mill must lose 7,500 yuan per month at the current market price." The representatives of the labor side were then asked for their opinion on the mill's fair price policy. They replied that the fair price policy implemented by the mill was not very convenient for workers who eat out, and the benefits for the workers were not universal. They still requested a rice subsidy. The committee reviewed the fact that the workers' request for a rice subsidy due to the high price of rice was legitimate, but the mill had already voluntarily implemented a fair price policy, which had already provided a solution for the impact of high rice prices on the workers. The rice subsidy problem had already been solved. Furthermore, after investigating the mill's fair price policy, it was found that the workers were indeed receiving real benefits, and the amount of the subsidy was also larger than that of other cotton mills run by Chinese merchants that provide rice subsidies. This shows that the mill is not indifferent to the workers' livelihood. The representatives of the labor side still insisted on issuing a rice subsidy on the grounds that it was inconvenient for workers who eat out to buy fair-priced rice, but the reason was insufficient and should be rejected. Although the representatives of the capital side stated to the committee that there was no limit to the period of the fair price policy and that they intended to suspend it only when the price of rice fell below 13 yuan, this should also be clearly stipulated to allow the workers to work with peace of mind. The committee decided to make a ruling as stated in the main points.

The Wage Increase for Stevedores at the Butterfield & Swire Wharf Resolved. 144

The stevedores on the Butterfield & Swire Company's wharf in Pudong requested a wage increase from the contractor, Chang Shunlianxin, due to the high cost of goods and the difficulty of living. This request was not met, resulting in a strike on the 25th of last month. The Bureau of Social Affairs mediated the dispute several times, but no resolution was reached. It is now learned that the bureau invited representatives from both sides to negotiate again the day before yesterday. The attitudes of the labor and capital sides were more moderate than before. As a result, the capital side agreed to increase the workers' daily wage by 120 cash, and to increase the night shift by 70 cash if there is no night meal. The capital side will also be responsible for collecting union dues on behalf of the union.

Department Order to Encourage Subscription to Coal Industry and Tobacco Bond 145

The Ministry of Finance instructed the Jiangsu Financial Commissioner's Office, stating, "For compliance, the Shanghai Coal Industry Association has submitted a telegram stating that coal tax is being forcibly collected with bond subscriptions, and non-standard receipts are being issued, requesting a cancellation order, etc. Upon investigation, this case was previously submitted, approved, and the relevant personnel instructed to comply. Now, based on previous information, except for the acknowledgment of the telegram, the bond subscription related to tax is proportional to the commodity tax, originally an equal method. How can the claim of distinction between poor and wealthy merchants be made? It is entirely incorrect. At this critical juncture of military progress, financial needs are extremely pressing, and bond subscription is of utmost urgency. The association is hereby tasked with earnestly guiding the fellow merchants, avoiding further excuses and evasion, which would resemble disrupting the bond drive, leading to unfavorable consequences. Regarding receipts, the Jiangsu Financial Commissioner has been strictly ordered again to instruct the Coal Tax Bureau to uniformly issue official printed receipts. In addition to the approval, it is hereby further ordered that the said personnel be instructed to comply accordingly. This order is hereby issued."

Blind Youth Attempts Suicide, Saved 148

Yesterday at half past noon, a blind youth was found attempting suicide by hanging himself from a telephone pole near Pengjiazhai, Lannidu, Pudong. Fortunately, Li Dianming, a patrol officer from the Third District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, was passing by and rescued him, saving his life. He was taken to the district for questioning. The youth stated his name was Wang Shunxing, 24 years old, from Gaoyou. He used to farm in his hometown, but was conscripted into the army and sent to Fujian. Later, due to physical weakness and blindness, he was released and sent back. Passing through Shanghai, he had no relatives or friends, and no money, facing starvation. Therefore, he resorted to suicide, etc. The district chief, considering his plight as a wanderer in a foreign land attempting suicide, found his situation particularly pitiable and ordered that a report be prepared and sent to the General Bureau for relief.

Silk Pongee Gown Recognized at Police Station 150

Confirmed as Stolen Property

Leading to the Arrest of a Thief

At 8:40 a.m. on the morning before yesterday, the home of Cheng Baishun, a local resident at No. 493-494 Fu'an Lane, North Zhejiang Road, was invaded by four thugs. Each held a handgun and first confined the family members to one room, forbidding them from making any noise. Then, they ransacked the boxes and chests, stealing seven yuan in cash, a gold watch, several pieces of clothing, and fled with the loot. At that time, detectives Liu Changgen and Ding Baoxiang from the Huisi Police Station, along with Chinese and foreign officers, were inspecting passing pedestrians and vehicles on North Shanxi Road. They saw a man wearing a light blue silk pongee gown who looked suspicious and searched him. A handgun with six live rounds was found on his person, and he was taken back to the police station. Coincidentally, Cheng Baishun was also reporting his home invasion to the police station. He inadvertently caught sight of the silk pongee gown and recognized it as stolen property. He then learned that the man was one of the four thieves. Upon questioning by the police chief, the man confessed his name was Qiang Yongxiang, a native of Wuxi. Yesterday, he was sent to the Special District Local Court for prosecution. Cheng's nephew, Xi Rong, also testified in court, confirming that the defendant was indeed the thief holding the gun at the scene. The police station's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, stated that the police station still needed to investigate and requested an extension. Judge Sun briefly questioned the defendant and ordered him to be detained, rescheduling the hearing for further investigation.

Dispute Over Leased Land in Yu Garden 151

Police Station No Longer Intervening

The Guihua Hall and neighboring Ji Shunxing Bird Shop and other houses and open space in the Yu Garden of the City God Temple belong to the Qingfen Tang of the old Flower Industry Association and are managed by Director Zhang Yuanmao. Since the fire in Guihua Hall, Zhang Yuanmao originally intended to rebuild it, but was opposed by other directors, resulting in years of litigation and no construction. Furthermore, because the adjacent houses and open space were leased to Ji Shunxing Bird Shop, etc., with fixed-term contracts, which have not yet expired, Jiang Heting (also known as Jiang Zhongyi) reported to the Second Precinct of the First District last month, deceptively requesting the police to order tenants such as Yu Guangyin and Ji Shunxing to move out immediately to facilitate renovation. As the shops stated that their lease contracts had not expired, they refused to move. Officer Ma summoned the staff of Ji Shunxing shop, ordering them to provide a guarantee and vacate the premises within seven days, or face consequences. Subsequently, Ji Hailan, the owner of the birdcage shop, Yu Guangyin, and various stallholders jointly sued the local court, stating that they had leased the houses and open space from the Qingfen Tang Association, all with leases that should be contractually binding. Jiang Heting has no relationship with the property, so how could he request the police station to order them to move out for renovation, etc.? The court held a joint hearing on the 28th of last month, but the defendant Jiang Heting did not appear, and the case was not concluded. Unexpectedly, the Second Precinct of the First District again instructed the police to summon Yu Guangyin and the various stallholders to the police station the day before yesterday (the 1st), asking why they refused to move. Yu Guangyin, etc., replied that they had already sued in the local court and that Jiang Heting had not appeared at the hearing despite having sufficient reasons, and was now deceptively seeking an order to move from the police station. But this is a civil lawsuit and should be adjudicated by the judicial authorities. Yu Guangyin, etc., accompanied the police to the station to explain the situation, and asked Officer Ma to hand Jiang Heting over to them to go to the local court for questioning, and presented a draft subpoena. Officer Ma, observing that the case was already in court, decided to wait for a verdict before handling it further, and allowed Yu Guangyin, etc., to leave.

Xin Qingying Robbed at Niutengjian 153

Pirates Searched Ship by Ship

Passenger's Lost Money Recovered

The Xin Qingying small steamer, a Pinghu-bound vessel of the Qingji Inland River Shipping Company at Beisuzhou Road, Pentang Lane Bridge North, was towing a company ship filled with passengers and cargo the day before yesterday (the 1st). It departed from Shanghai at around 4:00 PM and sailed to Niutengjian, east of Siputang. At around 10:00 PM, four pirate ships suddenly appeared, carrying more than twenty pirates. They shouted for the steamer to stop and fired four volleys of gunfire. The steamer's captain, Yang Xingdi, had no choice but to stop the engine. The pirates jumped onto the steamer and began searching. They stole 150 yuan in cash, two leather suitcases, four bundles of clothing, more than twenty quilts, silk, satin, foreign cloth, cigarettes, satin shoes, and fruits such as bananas from Yang Xingdi, worth seven or eight hundred yuan in total. After robbing the steamer, they boarded the company ship (Captain Qin A'gen) and stole 50 pounds of wool, 10 bottles of brandy, and a large leather suitcase (belonging to Zhu Xiangrui, being transported to Haiyan), and sailed away with the loot after firing a shot. The steamer was carrying two passengers, including a Mr. Yang from Haiyan who was doing business in Shanghai. His relative in his hometown had recently died of illness and was destitute. He received a urgent letter informing him that his relatives had passed but left nothing for a coffin and burial. Mr. Yang immediately raised 51 yuan in Shanghai to return home on the steamer to purchase a coffin and bury the relative. When he saw the pirates boarding the ship, he threw a packet of money in the cabin. It was later found by a ship worker, Mr. Jia. After the theft, Mr. Yang told the crowd about his situation, weeping. Mr. Jia inquired about the amount and the name of the bank, which matched. He took out the packet of money and returned it. Mr. Yang was overjoyed and took out five yuan to give to Mr. Jia as a reward, thanking him profusely. It was indeed fortunate. After the steamer was robbed, it continued to Pinghu. In addition to the ship's accountant, Ding Meijiang, reporting the incident to the local water police, the steamer also sailed to Zhujing on the way back and requested the army and police to send officers to investigate. The steamer arrived in Shanghai last night and reported the incident to the company for verification.

Rural Woman Induced, Raped, and Trafficked 154

Chen Tingfang, a young woman from Nantong, is 19 years old and married to Wang Qingzhang, a simple farmer. She has a son who is only seven months old. The woman is young and weak-willed, leading her to be induced to come to Shanghai by Wang Yiting. Initially, their relationship was very intimate, but once the money ran out, the man lost his face. Wang sold the child to someone for only six yuan, which was quickly spent. He then sold the woman to Lin Yuguang, who resided at No. 15, Lane 85, Jiangbian Wharf, as his wife for an agreed price of 60 yuan, with half paid in advance. Yesterday, Wang went to collect the rest of the money but was grabbed by the woman, who called the police and had him arrested by the Second District Police Station, who then handed him over to the Local Court. After a preliminary hearing by the prosecutor, Wang Yiting was ordered to be detained, while Chen Tingfang was temporarily detained pending notification of her family to claim her.

Investigation into a Fleeing Woman 155

Yang Chen, the young wife of Yang Guowen, a resident of Caojiadu in West Shanghai, had an affair with Gong Yonglin. The day before yesterday, she packed her clothes and hid in Gong's home in Sijiantou. However, Yang had already found out and had people lying in wait to arrest her. Yang Chen needed to change her clothes but could not retrieve them, so she asked Zhu Hongxiang, a male worker at the factory, to retrieve them for her. Zhu, who was only fifteen years old and unaware of the situation, happily went and was captured by Yang and others, who took him to the Police Station of the 86th district. Zhu explained the situation, and a senior police officer was immediately sent to the factory to arrest Yang Chen and take her to the police station. After clarifying the situation, she was ordered to be handed over to the Local Court for handling.

Fine for Illegally Operating Opium Den 156

French Concession police detectives discovered the day before yesterday that Wang Yanji, a resident, was illegally operating an opium den, allowing members of the lower classes to smoke opium pills. This not only violated the ban but also endangered people's lives. They raided the premises and seized the opium smoking paraphernalia and opium pills, taking them to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought before the French court for prosecution. Wang Yanji confessed that he illegally operated an opium den, and the Chinese and Western judges fined him 75 yuan, confiscated the proceeds, and confiscated the opium smoking paraphernalia and opium pills.

Opium Trafficker Caught En Route 157

Ji A'gen, an opium trafficker from Tongzhou, was found yesterday morning around 9:00 AM to be carrying opium on his person. He took a public bus and was getting off at Taoming Road when he was spotted by Chinese Constable No. 2310, who suspected his appearance. He was immediately stopped, and 25 taels of opium were found on Ji's person. He was taken to the Yangshupu Police Station and informed the police chief, who ordered him to be detained and sent to the Special District Court for questioning.

Weather Report 160

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated that the Yangtze River Basin and the coast here would be cloudy with rain and fog. There would be northeast winds over the Yellow Sea, east winds over the East Sea, and no directional winds on the Shandong coast. Also, the highest temperature in this port in the 24 hours before 3 p.m. yesterday was 84.2 and the lowest was 72.2. On the same day last year, the highest was 87.8 and the lowest was 71.4.
