Free Talk

A Laughing Matter 161

— Hai Ke

A: I've been having eye problems lately. When I read, one line turns into two.

B: Then you should quickly see an ophthalmologist for a diagnosis. Otherwise, how can you go out and do things?

A: No, I actually got a job because of it. The electric company heard that I could see one as two, so they hired me to take on the job of copying the meter readings. The salary is especially generous.

Telephone attendant: Our master is at home. Please wait a moment. There is no sound on the phone.

Attendant: Please wait a moment.

Person on the phone: Are you blind? I've been nodding here for a while!

A: I only saw your masterpiece at this exhibition.

B: Thank you. My painting is not good to look at. Didn't you look at anyone else's work?

A: There were too many people looking, and I couldn't squeeze in.

Child: Father, I love that little horse next door. What if I stole it?

Father: At least six months in jail.

Child: Then when I'm in jail, please take care of it for me, Father. Don't forget to feed it hay.

London Women Addicted to Smoking 162

— Qiu Shui

Today's cigarettes are like yesterday's opium. If you stroll through the streets, you will see women, children, and the elderly, almost everyone with a cigarette in their hand. Advocates are worried about this as if it is a dangerous flood. Civilized countries such as England and the United States have contacted three or four confidants to form a tobacco quitting alliance, rejecting tobacco thousands of miles away and treating it as an enemy. The intention is good. However, the law has no provision prohibiting smoking (except for opium). Society also sees smoking as a normal thing, without any moral sanctions. However, when women smoke, society often considers it immoral. Also, there are loud cries to strike it down. Is this gender equality? It is no wonder that London women are addicted to smoking.

Women's Smoking Advertisement: Based on the concept of gender equality, 20th-century London women have reversed their old habits and become addicted to smoking. Recalling decades ago, women's smoking was banned in England and the United States, especially in public places. Today, in London society, such bans are long gone. Whether it is in the home, in the park, on the street, or even in the theater or on public transport, you can often see men and women, young and old, holding cigarettes and shouting wildly without thinking it is strange. However, looking back at the United States, women's smoking is still regarded as a shameful thing. Upper-class women hate it like an enemy. In social situations, if there is a woman present, men must first apologize before smoking. Otherwise, it will be considered rude. American women do not smoke. Years ago, a major American newspaper published an advertisement for cigarettes, depicting a woman smoking. It was met with dissatisfaction from society at the time. Church groups even filed formal protests, forcing it to stop publishing before stopping.

The Queen's Smoking Breaks the Prohibition: The prevalence of cigarettes among London women is as described above. However, there is no one who knows the reason for its prevalence. However, according to those who are deeply familiar with London allusions, there are two major reasons that can be described. One is that the world's cigarette production is increasing day by day. In order to promote their business, a group of ingenious people invented a small cigarette a few years ago, which is specially for women to smoke. The taste is mild and the decoration is beautiful. A few women initially bought and smoked it out of curiosity. Over time, they became addicted. Now it is popular and is considered a habit. The second is that London women smoke. The British Queen is actually a severe ladder. Although London women have been using cigarettes extensively, they often do not dare to do so arbitrarily at royal garden parties. Because there is a queen, how can civilians dare to be so permissive? Unexpectedly, a few years ago, at a banquet hosted by a duke, the Queen also attended. In order to respect the Queen, the hostess had notified the guests in advance not to smoke in their seats. Unexpectedly, halfway through the banquet, the Queen suddenly stood up and looked for cigarettes everywhere. Unable to find any, she ordered her attendants to ask the hostess for them. The hostess was shocked and quickly prepared good cigarettes to give to her. Those guests who had a habit of smoking also took out what they had brought with them and smoked together. For a time, the smoke was thick, and everyone was happy. As a result, the Queen's smoking spread far and wide, and London women felt even less restrained about smoking.

Tidbits of Common Sense 163

— Zui Chi Sheng

Raw soy sauce is not suitable for consumption. It must be steamed in a rice pot. It is hygienic and not easy to mold.

If you encounter a chimney with fire and smoke, quickly soak salt in water and pour it into a high place, and the smoke and fire will extinguish by themselves.

When buying rice straw at home, be careful of the people who sell straw doing tricks. Generally, the straw that is fraudulent is cheaper than usual, and the form is fluffy and hollow. When weighing the straw, secretly insert the carrying bag into the two loops. Deliberately speaking and pointing to make people look at the head loop and the scale code. Approximately, each bundle of straw is more than twenty pounds, which can be weighed up to fifty pounds. As a result, you will suffer a great loss. If they are seen through, these people will not be willing to sell and leave. This is the secret of the straw sellers, which must be known.

Adding salt and alkali to boiling water and pouring it on the mattress can kill bedbugs and their eggs.

Guest of Honor Turns into Prisoner 164

— Liu Hate Me, From Hangzhou

The world is becoming more and more dangerous and cunning. Impersonation and deception are endless. Red figures of the party and the state are often impersonated by people who hold letters and pay visits. Relatives, colleagues, or people who introduce them to seek positions or make loans without permission. If the person in charge is careless, they will fall into their trap. The announcement by He Yingqin can be used as proof. A case of impersonating a letter to seek a position also occurred in Hangzhou a few days ago. It is really unique. There was a Wang Yun, also known as Bingquan, who paid a visit to Zhen Shaoshen, director of the Zhejiang Salt Affairs Anti-Smuggling Bureau. He claimed that he had come from the sea to visit Wen Yingxing, director of the Anti-Smuggling Office of the Ministry of Finance, who had asked him to come. He also presented a letter from Zou Lin, director of the Salt Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance, requesting that Wang be appointed as the captain of the anti-smuggling brigade. Director Zhen did not suspect anything at first and regarded it as a normal matter. However, because there was no suitable position at the time, he asked him to wait. Wang then left. A few days later, Director Zhen suddenly received a letter from Director Wen saying that Wang, who had come to seek a position, had replied to Director Zou. He said that Wang Yun had never been known before and had never been recommended. He was impersonating someone to seek advancement. He was afraid that he was not a good person. Please send the original letter back for investigation. On the one hand, please inform him not to give him a position or appointment to avoid trouble. After reading it, Director Zhen understood the situation and ignored it. However, yesterday, Wang came again, claiming that he had been waiting for a position for many days and had not been appointed, so he could not report Director Zou's orders. His words were quite indignant. He also said that if the brigade commander was not available for a while, he could also settle for the captain of the squadron and be promoted later. Director Zhen then asked if he knew Director Zou. Wang said yes. He had known him in Guangzhou and was an old friend of many years. When asked about the origin of the letter, he replied that he had personally asked Director Zou to give it to him in person. Director Zhen could not bear it any longer and smiled. Wang's face changed immediately upon hearing this. He was sternly questioned. He said that he did not know Director Zou well and only knew a secretary of the Salt Affairs Department named Chen Zepai. The letter was forwarded by Chen. Director Zhen carefully examined his tone and found that it was inconsistent. Moreover, most of the secretaries of the Salt Affairs Department were old friends, and there was no one named Chen Zepai. As a result, Wang's crime of impersonating the letter was confirmed, and he was immediately detained. At one time, the guest of honor became a prisoner. Wang was about thirty years old, dressed in a suit, spoke with an Anhui accent, and had a very beautiful appearance. It was said that he had served as the captain of the fourth squadron of the tenth brigade of the Zhejiang Anti-Smuggling Bureau. Later, he was removed for corruption. His actions this time were impersonating someone to seek advancement, and it was inevitable that his nature would be difficult to change. Director Zhen believed that this kind of behavior was not only harmful to Director Zou but also had a great impact on social credit. He planned to send him to court for punishment to warn others.

Azure Rice 165

— Xu Xiaoting

There are many types of rice. The rice husked from red glutinous rice seeds is red in color like rosy clouds. The rice of white Jingxian rice is as bright as white jade. No matter what type of rice it is, although the colors are different, its function of filling hunger is the same. Rice can relieve hunger, but I have never heard of rice with a color like blue-black. If the color of rice is like blue-black, then the rice will produce black ears. The rice grains that are formed will also become black rice? The strangeness of the matter is something that ordinary people cannot predict. In Shagou Town, Yancheng, farmer Chen has been farming dozens of acres of land. A Hunan friend gave him dozens of pounds of green rice seeds last year. Chen set aside a few acres of land to plant the rice this spring. When the autumn season comes, the rice has matured. The rice ears that are formed in this field are obviously ready to be harvested. However, although the rice stalks are withered and yellow, the rice grains are green in color like blue-black. In addition to being surprised, Chen peeled open a few grains to look at them. The rice grains had grown, but they were green and not white. So, he harvested the rice a few days ago, dried it in the sun, and husked more than one load to cook. To his surprise, the cooked porridge had large rice grains, but they were green in color like green jade, similar to mung bean soup. When eaten, it was similar to ordinary rice porridge. However, it had a slight aroma. When the neighbors heard about it, they all asked Chen for some to eat. They all said that this rice was a different kind of grain. Its body was soft and large, making it easiest to digest for the elderly. The nearby machine organs learned about this and specially bought a few loads from Chen to use as a reference for agricultural seeds.

Occasional Notes on Listening to Songs 166

— Wei Weiyi

In previous years, when I traveled to the old capital, I had nothing to do. Apart from buying wine and getting drunk, I often entertained myself by watching operas. The pool seats were extremely cheap, and the performers were excellent. Sometimes they were veteran performers from the imperial troupe, or newly debuted young talents. They sang stories of the Kaiyuan era and tales of the Tianbao era. With the wild goose zither and ivory clappers, my heart was filled with joy. Over time, it became a habit that I could not break. Later, when I came to Shanghai, I became a book copyist. My eyesight grew weaker and weaker. The theaters in Shanghai competed to display elaborate scenery, resplendent and colorful. Because my eyesight was poor and I lacked leisure time, I rarely went to see them. However, I developed a fondness for records. The lyrics of records, though extremely simple, were selected from the best parts of an opera, so every word was precious and worth listening to. The singers were either famous performers or famous amateurs. They had years of practice and could produce a stunning performance. Their voices could stop the clouds, enough to curb my addiction to opera and allow me to focus on research. I often purchased records from the Victor Talking Machine Company on Nanjing Road, sometimes as many as one hundred or more. They covered a wide range of roles: male, female, painted-face, and clown. Among them, those produced by Gaoting were the most numerous. Male roles were sung by Shu Yan, Qing Kui, Lian Liang, and Ju Ming. Female roles were sung by Shi Tou, Lan Fang, Yan Qiu, and Xiao Yun. Painted-face roles were sung by Gui Xian and Jun Feng (a record of Liu Po was especially rare). Clown roles were sung by Chang Hua and He Nian. The male roles were subtle and restrained, neither humble nor arrogant. The female roles were like long embankments and willow waves, newly tested oriole tongues. The painted-face roles were like the yellow bell and great lu, iron clappers and bronze drums. The clown roles were witty and humorous, extremely funny. Although I was in a small room, it was as if I had moved the talents of the northern lands and created a grand stage. Regarding Shi Tou and Liu Po, who have both passed away, I can still listen attentively to their recorded voices, as if they were right here. I truly have to give credit to records. I look north towards Yan Yun, using this to console myself. Therefore, I write this record.

Inside Story of the Increase in Unemployed Workers in England (Part 2) 168

— Li Liuzeng, sent from Paris

According to the statistics of the Times, since 1921, the cost of living has decreased by approximately 22.5%. During the same period, the rate of unemployment relief has increased by 13% for single men and 30% for married men with three children. Agricultural workers are the most impoverished and fertile class in England. They have no land and rely solely on their labor to support their families. Currently, if an agricultural worker is the father of three children, he can receive 32 shillings per week in unemployment relief, while he would only earn 35 shillings per week when working. It is human nature to love ease and hate labor. Would anyone prefer to work hard all day for an extra three shillings a week?

Let me cite a specific example as proof. A servant and his wife were both employed in a mansion, earning 100 to 120 pounds per year. After much deliberation, the servant suddenly resigned with his wife. When asked why, he replied that after careful calculation, the man would not work at all. His wife would only work part-time for two or three days a week. Their combined income would be better than before. Examples like this are too numerous to count.

Currently, British public opinion is criticizing the Unemployment Insurance Act established by the Labour cabinet this year, saying that the qualifications for receiving relief are too broad and the amount of relief is too large. This causes many workers to have wishful thinking, trying to avoid work and live without labor. This not only poses a risk of bankruptcy to the British economy but also contributes to the decline of national morality. According to various newspapers, in order to thoroughly solve the unemployment problem and save British industry, it is necessary to amend the social insurance law. Genuine unemployed workers should be given relief, but only enough to maintain their livelihood, and the payment of relief should be conditional on having fully paid into the insurance fund when employed. However, the various political parties have responded to this kind of proposal with a lukewarm attitude, unwilling to express any opinion. Why? Because it involves domestic politics, and any change would have a huge impact. Furthermore, they fear that this would cause resentment among workers, which would be very unfavorable to the party's future.

In conclusion, the solution to the unemployment problem in England depends on the revitalization of the world economy and the recovery of the Eastern market, but it is also closely related to domestic reforms. However, reforming domestic affairs requires long-term efforts and unwavering courage. Therefore, the MacDonald cabinet's current headache of two million unemployed workers is unlikely to be resolved in the near future.

The father of the pitiful Cui Yun was both an honest man and a fool. Even if he had something to say, his wife's loud voice would scare away two of his three souls, and he wouldn't dare to say another word. And his daughter entered the hell of the brothel. Speaking of selling young children from good families into prostitution in Shanghai, there are various systems. Some are outright sales, some are pledges for ten years, some are pledges for three or five years, and some are package deals for a certain period. In short, it's all a life of imprisonment. Outright sales are like life imprisonment without parole. Ten years, five years, and three years are like fixed-term imprisonment. Even a package deal for a certain period is like doing hard labor for four months. However, the state establishes penalties to punish criminals. I ask, what crimes have those innocent and lovely little girls committed to deserve such suffering? Isn't this an injustice in society? Cui Yun was pledged to someone by Sister Xiu for ten years, starting from the age of fourteen and lasting until the end of her twenty-third year. This ten-year fixed-term imprisonment is almost equivalent to life imprisonment. Think about it, a woman's youth is entirely within those ten years. Those ten years are wasted in a life of imprisonment. Her life can be considered over. The family that takes the pledge also has to spend some money to feed her, clothe her, and teach her songs. When she reaches the legal age of sixteen, they have to put up a sign and have her sing on stage. Fortunately, if the child is obedient and the family is kind, she will suffer less. Otherwise, she will be beaten and scolded day and night, becoming as thin as a ghost. Many of them die from illness. There are countless such small wronged souls. Under duress, they receive those who indulge in bestial desires, disregarding humanity and breaking their maidenhood. The serious ones die, and the less serious ones suffer lifelong illnesses. Those things are commonplace. However, Cui Yun was lucky. She didn't lose her chastity until she was eighteen. The guest originally wanted to marry her, but unfortunately, there was also a shrew at home, so there was nothing he could do. He had to make up for this regret with money. He helped Cui Yun redeem herself. It can be seen that the life in the brothel is completely like the criminal system. Money is used as a ransom, and crimes can be redeemed with money. Their unwritten rules are to redeem at double the price. For example, if she was bought for three hundred dollars, it would cost six hundred dollars to redeem her. The same goes for pledges. In this case, someone needs to help, or consult a lawyer who protects flowers, or let the old men at their illegal court, the so-called tea party, decide whether to allow you to redeem yourself and be free. Otherwise, they will hold onto your body, and they can use any means. Because if they marry you off, it will be at least three thousand or five thousand dollars. In any case, it will be more than just double the redemption fee. Cui Yun was also lucky that this guest secretly helped her gain a little freedom.

Cotton Yarn: The Yarn Market Remains Mediocre 175

The yarn market is calm, but the trend is still softening. The domestic war is unstable, the purchasing power of all parties is weak, and the raw cotton is sluggish, so the situation is flat. The pressure on the selling side is increasing, and the buyers are relatively scarce. Most targets must look at breaking through the 50 tael mark. It is found that new throwing households have not been enthusiastic in the recent market, so although the environment is bad, the decline has not been fierce and may be able to hover for the time being.

The Human Standard Emotion is Extremely Flat. The early opening of the Human Standard was weak due to the lack of buyers and the weakness of the market atmosphere. Han Standard Market Strongly Rises on All Sides 176

The cotton market remains firm, likely because the weather is sometimes cloudy and sometimes sunny, making people's minds unsettled. Both American and Indian cotton have suspended trading, so the buying force is becoming stronger, resulting in a tighter market. However, new buyers are still lacking, and current cotton sales are unusually sluggish. Factories are taking a calm approach, and so are the Japanese factories. In previous years, at this time, Japanese merchants would be eagerly collecting cotton, but this year Indian cotton has been sufficient, so there is no need for temporary procurement. Osaka's Three Commodities market for yarn and cotton is flat and weak. A major yarn factory in this port received a telegram from its Hankou branch stating that it had rained there for three days, but now the weather has cleared up, and the new cotton harvest looks promising.

Standard Tightening - The Hankou standard market opened with most people expecting a high price, and buyers taking a strong and rising attitude, so the market atmosphere was tight. However, there were not many new buyers, resulting in a flat outcome. In the afternoon, the market opened with rain, and the bulls raised the price again by 1 cent. At closing, news of poor American cotton caused the price to fall again, resulting in a near rise of 5 cents to 1 cent, then a fall of 5 cents. The total daily trading volume was 23,300 dan.

Food - Rice Market Gradually Rises 178

Zhabei - Yesterday, very few boats arrived from the river, and the demand from various gangs was quite strong. The price of Northern Gang white broken rice reached 21 yuan in bulk, reaching the limit price. Ordinary Zhongguan rice all rose by 2-3 jiao or so. It is noted that the recent market situation for japonica rice is influenced by the production market in the interior, and the new goods could not continue to be strong. In addition, many foreign rice shipments were re-exported, and inventories were thin. Although there is a rumor of Xianggan rice being wholesaled to Shanghai, there is currently no certainty, leading to a sharp rise in prices. Very few East Xin japonica rice arrived, and rice mills showed a weak willingness to sell, so the market improved again by 3-5 jiao, with the opening price at 18.45 yuan, and ordinary rice at 18.12 yuan, with very strong buying interest. New Ke Xian rice is ostensibly hovering around 14 yuan, but in reality, medium-quality rice has risen by about 2 jiao. These goods are readily accepted upon arrival, but only customers are inquiring, leading to a shift from flat to tight. Thin rice sales are acceptable, but arrivals are scarce and lack luster, so the market is slightly firmer. The White Yuan market is unfavorable, as the price has risen too sharply in recent days, leading to a lack of buying interest, while cargo merchants inevitably hold a desire to sell quickly. As a result, the bulk price has fallen slightly by 1-2 jiao, with high-quality goods still around 19 yuan.

Hu Nan - Fewer boats continue to arrive from the river. Buyers in this street are not paying attention due to the slight cargo volume. Although they are slightly selective in their purchases, transactions inevitably become thinner. High-quality broken rice is increasingly quiet. Prices have no standard because sources are intermittent, so they mostly follow the Beishi market. As for medium and lower-quality goods, there is also only slight trading, and the trend is still good. The market surface shows an increase of 1-2 jiao, with goods like Tongli rice all in the range of 17.8 yuan. New japonica rice sources are slightly visible, and sales are very good, with prices gradually rising by half a yuan, opening at 18-17.5 yuan. New Yangjian rice arrivals and sales are evenly matched, with most being sold out as soon as they arrive. High-quality goods are around 15 yuan, about 1.5 jiao higher than the previous market. White Yuan inventories and arrivals are both scarce, and the market is very quiet, with prices similar to those in Hu Bei.

Tapioca Flour Market Continues to Show Weakness 179

Yesterday, the tapioca flour market, after opening in the morning and afternoon, the market for each month still showed signs of weakness, and trading was also exceptionally sluggish. Because Tianjin has changed to ordering foreign flour due to food-related reasons after Shanghai flour was banned from loading. Foreign firms are also selling because the exchange rate is close, and they are directly delivered, so the Shanghai market is actually being blocked from sales. Although manipulators are not completely disheartened and unwilling to let go, in fact, the support of Shanghai flour and the inability to export indirectly add a new path for foreign flour to come to China. If the factory throws down more weight or the market situation becomes flat, the result will be fatigue. In the end, this month is down a little 0.25 cents, October is down a little 0.75 cents, November and December are down a little 0.5 cents, January is down a little 0.75 cents, and February is down a little 1.5 cents.

Wheat Futures Market Unanimously Slackens 180

Yesterday, the wheat futures market, after opening in the morning and afternoon, the market for each month all showed a flat and weak trend. The current month saw a continuous arrival of goods, and in view of the fearful repetition of the previous month, the bulls were weak and unbearable. Although there was no price quotation for foreign wheat for the deferred months, the need for wheat may be reduced due to Tianjin's continuous ordering of foreign flour, so people are also very pessimistic. As a result, the current month is down a little 1 cent compared to the previous day, October to January are down a little 2 cents, and February is up 1 cent. In the spot wheat market, high-quality goods were called up by 1-2 cents due to the continued movement of factories, while medium and lower-quality goods remained flat. 6,500 packages of Taierzhuang, Xuzhou Yao, Shashi, and Haizhou wheat were opened and purchased by Fufeng and Shen Da.

Silk and Tea - Zhejiang Hangzhou Autumn Silkworm Season is Quite Good 184

Currently, the Majority of Leaves are Lush... Early Silkworms Can Emerge from the Fire

Farmers in the four rural areas of Hangzhou County, Zhejiang Province, are breeding autumn silkworms due to the profits made from spring and summer silkworms this year. In addition, silk merchants are promoting and government offices are distributing silkworm eggs, doubling the amount of feeding. After the ants were collected, the climate was suitable, and the silkworm ants developed smoothly. Although there were strong winds, thunderstorms, and sudden cold and heat, the impact was minimal due to the running and guidance of instructors. Currently, the majority of leaves are lush, and early silkworms can emerge from the fire, and the silkworm season is quite good.

Tea merchants generally hold deep worries about this market situation.

Market News 214

Yongan Company's stationery department declares: Since the stationery department moved to the east end, the wholesale business has become extremely developed. Recently, several female employees have been hired to specialize in selling fountain pens and beautiful imitation paper flowers. A large batch of stationery and decorative supplies have recently been shipped from Europe and the United States, coinciding with the company's 12th anniversary special sale. For example, the American Conklin forever-guaranteed pen, available in several colors, originally priced at 14 yuan and 40 cents per pen, is now limited to 500 pens during the big sale period, priced at 9 yuan, 80 cents, and 5 cents per pen, with an additional warranty, free replacement of new parts, and permanent free service. German large tin box watercolor paints, 70 cents and 5 cents per box; No. 2, 50 cents per box; German Axe Brand pencils, 30 cents per dozen; school bags, 60 cents per bag; pencil sharpeners, 7 cents per piece; French 46-inch wide oil painting canvas, 10 yuan per bolt; this brand of crepe paper, 10 cents per bolt; art paper lanterns, dozens of types, 20 cents to 1 yuan and 20 cents and 5 cents per piece. These lanterns are extremely beautiful when displayed in shop windows and living rooms. Five-color printed paper tape, 20 cents and 5 cents per bolt; printed crepe paper, 30 cents and 40 cents per bolt. In addition, stationery, envelopes, oil paints, watercolor paints, various drawing papers and canvases, and high-quality inkwells are all available, with special big sales, etc.

Jingan Craft Studio in Changxing Lane, Jielu Road, declares: The director of our studio, Mr. Zheng Jingan, previously returned to Guangdong after being hired, planning to set up a soap factory. He has been away from Shanghai for a long time, but now he has returned and will continue to teach the manufacture of various daily and cosmetic industrial products as usual. In addition, the "Experimental Household Industrial Manufacturing Lecture Compilation" published by our studio is now on sale at a special price of one yuan. The content includes dozens of manufacturing methods for laundry soap, transparent scented soap, fruit dew, and various cosmetics, etc.

Liangyou Clothing Company, newly established at the intersection of Laobazi Road and Fusheng Road, declares: Our company has specially hired experienced technicians, carefully selecting exquisite and high-quality materials, and finely crafting the latest style Western suits and clothing, offering preferential treatment to gentlemen from all walks of life, with affordable prices. The interior is currently being renovated and will be officially opened soon.

Theater News 215

Xindongfang Theater, located north of Yokohama Bridge on North Sichuan Road, declares: Our theater has magnificent architecture and complete organization, making it the most suitable and comprehensive stage of the modern era. It aims to promote national opera and emerging opera. The directors are all prominent figures and celebrities in the theater industry, and the preparations have taken years to complete. It has now been decided to open on September 3rd, starting at 7:30 pm, with performances of improved national opera and opera. The national opera program is a sorrowful factual drama "The Female Escort," written by Hu Shaoyu and directed by Feng Zihe, starring Ms. Min Cuiying. The plot is completely realistic, with touching beauty and spectacle. The entire play features more than 30 actors and requires more than two hours to perform. There are also six magnificent stage sets, matched with reasonable costumes and beautiful music, making it interesting and captivating. The opera program is a historical story drama "Wang Zhaojun," starring Ms. Li Lian from the [unclear] Society. The plot is tragic and the songs are moving, containing literary poetry and great value. The ticket prices are also extremely affordable, ranging from 40 cents, 60 cents, 80 cents, and one yuan. It is expected that there will be a bustling scene with carriages and horses at that time.

Lianyi Film Company declares: Our company has been preparing for more than a year, and all the progress has been properly arranged. It is now scheduled to start shooting the martial arts adventure epic "Tai Chi Dart," written by playwright Li Changjian, on the 5th of this month. The plot is bizarre and tortuous, completely breaking the hypocrisy of gods and monsters with real martial arts skills. Mr. Li spent one and a half years of painstaking effort writing this script, revising it seven or eight times. In addition, it stars the strongman Zha Ruilong and the long-famous movie star Ran Saizhen, truly a perfect match, opening a new era for domestic films. The company's office is temporarily located at 245 Yipin Lane, Baoshan Road, Zhabei.

Paris Grand Theater declares: Starting today, we will screen "Passionate Courageous Love Crossing the Sea to Avenge Injustices," co-starring Ramon Novarro and Joan Crawford. The film tells the story of two brothers who misunderstand each other because of a woman, leading to animosity. Later, the younger brother crosses the sea to Singapore to explain the misunderstanding, but unfortunately, the elder brother is killed by a villain. The plot is tortuous and full of twists and turns, with both humor and solemnity. The wonderful scenery of the sea is rarely seen by the world, and the mysterious images in Singapore's dance halls and bars are even more worth seeing.

Therefore, we have specially continued to stage the second part, with colorful scenery and mechanisms, striving for perfection, novelty, and mystery, creating a new record in the stage industry. There are also real dogs on stage, who know the rhythm, and fake horse performances, which closely resemble real horses. All kinds of peculiarities are pleasing to the eye. It is scheduled to be performed on Thursday evening this week. In recent days, many people have been coming to reserve seats, one after another, knowing that there will be a sea of people and a sensation in Shanghai at that time.

China Grand Theater on Zha Pu Road and Hai Ning Road declares: Since its opening, our theater has been well-received by the public due to its careful selection of films, and the business has been very prosperous. Yesterday, we changed to "Little Bush," a masterpiece co-starred by the three major stars Eddie Cantor, Clara Bow, and Lidorof. Incoming Mail 216

Respectfully Seeking a Formula for Stomach Cancer

My wife has stomach cancer, cannot eat, and medicine is ineffective. She vomits blue-green and coffee-colored water mixed with white greasy substances like phlegm several times a day, which is extremely painful. According to Western medicine, this disease is caused by a tumor in the stomach and must be surgically removed to have a chance of survival. However, my wife has both wet fever and stomach cancer. The wet fever has now completely healed, but her body is extremely weak. It has been more than 40 days since the onset of the disease, and she has not eaten. How can such a weak body withstand surgery? However, I cannot bear to sit and wait for her to die. Therefore, I am specially publishing this notice to seek kind-hearted famous doctors and request a good formula that can bring her back to life. If you can help, I will never forget your kindness for generations to come. If you have any advice, please send it to the Accounting Department of the China Merchants Bureau in Shanghai, addressed to me as a thank you. Wu Bo'an respectfully bows.

Social News

Records of Hermits Beyond the Sky 217

A Field Survey of Travel in Northern Europe - Unimaginable Fairy Mountains on the Sea

A special correspondent for the World News Agency in Northern Europe writes: The Western words "Suede" for Sweden and "Suisse" for Switzerland share the same origin. Their meaning probably implies seclusion. To translate them into Chinese with the closest sound and meaning, Sweden should be called 遯國 (Dùn Guó, "Secluded Country" - the character 遯 quite closely matches the sound of "Sweden"). The tranquility of Switzerland is most appropriately described as 隱國 (Yǐn Guó, "Hidden Country"). When transportation was underdeveloped in the Middle Ages, these two countries, with their dense forests, were convenient for avoiding chaos. During the recent outbreak of the European War, neither Sweden nor Switzerland was drawn into the conflict. The great powers seemed to forget about them, allowing the people of these two countries to enjoy the happiness of peace alone. Deep in the clouds and mountains, undisturbed by the sounds of chickens and dogs, like a paradise on earth, unexpectedly reappearing today - truly enviable! The meaning of "Norvege" for Norway is "Northern Country," a new nation that separated from Sweden. Although it doesn't have a name implying seclusion on the surface, in reality, it is still part of the "Secluded Country." However, its northern end has Nordkapp, a city where the sun never sets during the summer, making it even further north than the "Secluded Country." China is the country with the most troubles in the world. The Chinese people, separated by countless mountains, naturally cannot imagine the tranquility of the Northern Countries. Except for ten years ago when the International Women's Conference was held in Os-lo, the capital of the Northern Country, when Ms. Luo Kang Tongbi, the Chinese representative, selected scenic spots and wrote poems, there has been no news since, and no one has remembered this human paradise for a long time. The Chinese people have endured much turmoil and do not have the fortune to travel to this peaceful country, not even in their dreams. Isn't this regrettable? According to Mr. He Yuesun, who has preached and lectured in various Northwest European countries, "In places like Sweden and Norway, there are almost no Chinese footprints. When I worked for the Norwegian Youth Association, I traveled all over the country's cities. Over the years, I only found three Chinese people. One was a Cantonese man named Xiang Lin, with the Western name Andreas Tang Wa, who had lived in Norway for over twenty years but could not speak Norwegian. His livelihood was extremely difficult. I helped raise money to buy him a small boat so he could fish by the sea to make a living. He lived in a poor area, and his housing was rent-free, so he could barely survive. Another person, surnamed Huang (or Wang, it's hard to tell), was bought by a French circus performer to go to Europe. Unable to endure the hardship, he escaped midway. At the time, he was only eight years old and could no longer speak Chinese. The Norwegians helped him enter school, and he can now speak the local dialect and works in a restaurant. The third person was a woman who married a Norwegian sailor and lived in a small seaside village. Her family was quite comfortable. She could speak English, quite grammatically, and also Norwegian. She seemed to have received a better education. She claimed her father was a governor and hated the Republic of China. He once asked her for a small photo, but she said that she followed her mother's teaching, 'After marrying, follow your husband. Without her husband's permission, she cannot give away photos.' When I traveled to Sweden, I also found three Chinese people. One was Mr. Zhongzhang, the son of the former ambassador, Mr. Chaisheng, who lived with his remarried mother. He was studying various languages, and his environment was very good. The second was Miss Zhao, a former Manchu bannerwoman stationed in Jingzhou, who fled to Europe with a foreign missionary during the war. She is now in school studying general subjects. The third person was a Korean woman named Choi Young-sook, who was excellent in Chinese and also fluent in Swedish. She recently graduated from the social service college introduced by the Swedish church. Judging from her usual words and deeds, she is determined to become a Chinese citizen. These six people, alone, during the days when China was filled with war, peacefully lead a hermit's life in Scandinavia north of the ocean, rarely interacting with outsiders, giving people the feeling of 'Only in this mountain, where clouds are deep and unknown.' I remember that a senior colleague in our newspaper once used the pseudonym 'Secluded Elder of the Southern Sky' because he had experienced so much upheaval. Now, like the six people mentioned above, living peacefully in Sweden and Norway in the northern part of the Scandinavian Peninsula, no matter what their environment is, they are all leisurely 'Hermits North of the Mountain.' As for Denmark, in the southern part of the Scandinavian Peninsula, there are many overseas Chinese and frequent interactions, unlike the 'Secluded Country' that can sever ties with the world." (Correspondent: Shan Ren)

2.5 Million Unemployed in the United States 218

With Various Exceptions, the Total Number is Very Large

New York News: The US government announced that, according to a census in April, the total number of unemployed in the United States was more than 2.5 million, or 2% of the total population, and 5.5% of the total labor force. The highest unemployment rate was in Michigan, which includes the automobile industry center of Chicago. New York State had 365,000 people. In absolute numbers, this is about one-sixth of the total of 2.5 million. Although far less than the predicted 3 million to 6 million, this survey had various exclusions, such as: (1) Those who have the ability to work, although not unemployed, but have not received wages and have been on long-term leave. This was the most common situation, especially among coal miners, which is actually the same as unemployment. (2) Those who are in the same situation as the above but are on short-term leave. (3) Unemployed people who are unable to work due to illness. (4) Those who are unemployed but are not currently urgently seeking employment. (5) Unemployed people who have other income and do not worry about food and clothing. The total number of unemployed since April, including the above items, will reach a huge number. As Mr. Raibik, the director of the New York City Free Employment Agency, said, there are 250,000 unemployed union members in the city alone. Including those outside the union, the total will reach 500,000.

Britain and the United States Strive to Expand Their Air Forces 219

And Compete to Build Excellent Ships

Tokyo News: Although the British Naval Conference stipulated a treaty on auxiliary vessels for Britain, the United States, and Japan, the tendency of various countries to expand their air forces and compete to build excellent ships outside the treaty has gradually become apparent. Currently, the Japanese Navy is seeking to strengthen its naval aviation forces to counter the United States. This trend is also extremely enthusiastic in Britain and the United States, and the government and the public are eagerly seeking to strengthen it. The following is a record of the naval aviation policies and current status of military strength of Britain and the United States.

Britain

The Air Force is unified under the Air Ministry and divided into domestic and overseas forces, including naval cooperation teams and army cooperation teams. The aviation policy aims to defend against the French Air Force's military strength. Among them, the naval cooperation team aims for the US Navy and seeks to expand and prepare it. On the one hand, it emphasizes rapid transportation and communication and troop movement on territories spread all over the world, and strives to improve the mobility of aircraft. For example, the UK-India, UK-Australia, and UK-Africa connection flights are examples of this. The military strength is 74 squadrons, including 11 fleet aviation squadrons, with 85 first-line aircraft, 54 reserve aircraft, for a total of 1,390 aircraft. Among them, there are 150 fleet aircraft. It is planned to increase the independent squadrons for domestic defense to 52 squadrons by 1930, and to increase the fleet aviation squadrons to approximately 200 aircraft by the end of 1931. In addition, there are two large rigid airships, R-100 and R-101, which have recently completed air entry. The Air Force budget for 1929 was 6.2 million pounds.

United States

Unlike Britain's unified Air Force, the Navy and Army each have directly affiliated aviation units, like Japan. The aviation policy aims to be the world's number one and is steadily seeking to strengthen it. The policy of naval aviation equipment is to prioritize the strengthening of fleet aviation squadrons. The current military strength of the fleet aviation squadrons is 30 squadrons. The land-based units equipped in Hawaii and the Panama area and other important locations are approximately 20 squadrons. The naval aviation squadrons are 10 squadrons, for a total of 60 squadrons. There are also 10 reserve aviation squadrons. The number of aircraft is approximately 1,000 first-line aircraft. In addition, it has been decided to build two rigid large airships of 6 million cubic feet, larger than the German Xu Bolin and British R-100, one of which has already begun construction. The naval aviation budget for 1930 is 31.34 million gold dollars. By the end of 1931, the US naval aviation aircraft will have 1,000 first-line units. According to the provisions of the London Treaty, one-quarter of the total tonnage of cruisers under 10,000 tons can be equipped with flight decks. If the US Navy equips these ships with aircraft, the number will increase further. The greatness of the United States' aircraft manufacturing capacity is unparalleled in the world. It is said that during a national mobilization, it can produce 15,000 aircraft in the first twelve months.

Central European Countries Conduct Agricultural Cooperation Movement 220

Nine Countries Plan to Establish an Association

Budapest News: Yugoslavia, Romania, and Hungary recently sent representatives to Sinaia to discuss methods of cooperative sales of agricultural products in order to resist the competition of American agricultural products in the European market. Poland supported this move and submitted a memorandum advocating the establishment of an international agricultural agreement by nine Central European countries. The memorandum was delivered to the Hungarian Ministry of Foreign Affairs by the Polish Ambassador to Hungary, Mr. Bapingsiji. The content roughly stated that the current sluggish agricultural market cannot be salvaged without an international association. For this purpose, a conference should be held among Bulgaria, Estonia, Finland, Hungary, Lithuania, Romania, Czechoslovakia, Yugoslavia, and Poland to discuss and formulate methods for self-defense. Poland also proposed that these nine countries establish a permanent agricultural secretariat in Geneva to represent the nine countries when discussing agricultural issues. Yugoslavia expressed sympathy for this proposal. Its Foreign Minister, Mr. Malinkovic, is drafting a plan. At the same time, grain exporters from Southern Hungary and Romania also met to discuss this issue, advocating the establishment of a central organization to promote agricultural products. Bulgaria has expressed its willingness to join.

Britain's Economic Situation Deteriorates Daily 221

The High Unemployment is Unexpected - Railway Unrest is Brewing

London News: The number of unemployed people in Britain has recently increased again. Unemployment usually increases after the bank holiday in August each year, but this time it actually increased to 39,270 people, which was unexpected. Currently, the total number of unemployed people in Britain has exceeded any previous unemployment figures except during the coal miners' strike in 1921. The government and the Liberal Party are still secretly negotiating a new policy to deal with unemployment, but the public is not optimistic about the outcome. There is currently a trend to reduce unemployment benefits by two shillings per week. Railway companies are implementing large-scale layoffs due to reduced railway revenue, and unrest is brewing among railway personnel.

Japan's Population Trends Last Year 222

Divorces Increase, Marriages Decrease - Births Decrease, Deaths Increase

Tokyo News: According to the population trends released by the Japanese Cabinet Statistics Bureau last year, the natural increase in population was 815,798 people, approximately equivalent to the population of Wakayama Prefecture. The number of marriages was approximately 500,000, showing a gradual decreasing trend. The number of divorces was approximately 50,000, a slight increase compared to the previous year. Both births and deaths decreased compared to the previous year. The number of deaths increased. Including colonies, the total number of population trends is as follows:

Marriages: 502,483; Divorces: 51,726; Births: 2,122,201; Stillbirths: 17,541; Deaths: 1,283,896.

German Industrial Association Pays Attention to Agriculture 223

Establishes a Three-Year Plan of 100 Million Marks

Berlin News: The Hamburg German Industrial Association recently paid attention to the development of agriculture and established a three-year plan to use more than 100 million marks to improve cultivation conditions and promote agricultural product sales. The content includes five items as follows:

(1) Wheat must be grown more. 10% of the land in Central and Western Germany must be used for wheat.

(2) Reclaim wasteland and turn it into fertile land. Plant trees on dry sandy land.

(3) Rice may not be imported without the permission of the Association in order to protect the market for domestic rice. Rice must be graded according to quality and priced appropriately.

(4) Next year, establish a one-year milk association to greatly reduce the production price of milk. Change to new methods of raising cattle.

(5) Farmers and pig farmers should each organize associations.

Canada's Trade with China Develops 224

Due to Increased Imports of Wheat Flour

Canada's trade with China has shown significant development in recent years. The main reason is the increase in Chinese consumption of wheat flour. Before the European War, the value of Chinese exports to Canada was greater than Canadian exports to China. Recently, the opposite has occurred. An examination of the country's export trade to China in 1929 (fiscal year) shows that the total amount was 22.317 million gold dollars, of which wheat flour accounted for 11 million gold dollars, followed by silver at 3.37 million gold dollars. Other major exports to China were fish at 1 million gold dollars, timber at 330,000 gold dollars, automobiles at approximately 100,000 gold dollars, and paper and lead tin also had considerable amounts.

Automotive News

Commentary

The Evolution of the Truck 225

— Ji Ren

From Flower Car to Armored Car

When automobiles first appeared, passenger cars were viewed as "flower cars" (i.e., parade cars). Only wealthy merchants and powerful figures could afford to purchase them. Their purpose was simply out of curiosity. Riding in automobiles was considered a new form of entertainment. Now, however, automobiles have become a modern transportation tool. Even luxurious automobiles are inexpensive, and ordinary people can afford them.

Trucks were even later to develop. They have only been in circulation for thirty years. Because of their sturdiness and economy, they have long been used as transportation tools. As for how the first truck was manufactured, what it looked like, and whether it utilized a passenger car or another vehicle to install a motor to power it, there is no way to study it now.

According to most speculations, the earliest trucks were built by carriage makers. The wooden body contained an engine, driving gears, and a cargo bed. In reality, it was similar to a parade car.

This type of transportation vehicle had limited capacity and a narrow range of uses. Therefore, there was a motivation to promote mechanized trucks for construction to meet emergency needs, to transport food, livestock, oil, coal, bricks, stones, ammunition, money, lumber, and various other items. There was also a need for various types of chassis and bodies for businesses and stores to suit their needs, so that they could get satisfactory, fast, and stable service. Special modifications were also possible.

Now, taking the transportation of food and livestock as an example, ten years ago, the milk supply for major cities relied on trains and small carts. Today, however, all food, rice, wheat, flour, vegetables, and livestock are transported by trucks. Now, various companies and factories not only use trucks as an economical and fast means of transportation, but also use them as mobile advertisements throughout the city. The widespread use and effectiveness of trucks are now well known to everyone.

In addition to trucks, there are now escort vehicles, commonly known as armored cars. The steel-shelled body is fully armed to transport gold, silver, stocks, precious metals, and valuable items. The ones used by large banks and companies in major cities today are specially equipped to be safe and secure, without any chance of loss. The latest trucks are escort vehicles with fast speed, sturdy bodies, low and wide chassis, and sufficient weight. The window glass and windshield glass are bulletproof and will never shatter. The front and rear doors are tightly locked and blocked by iron bars. The rear door cannot be opened unless the front door is activated. It is managed by a guard to prevent the driver's conspiracy, thereby ensuring the driver's safety. The roof and rear of the car are equipped with machine guns to prevent robbery and resist unexpected attacks. The evolution of trucks can be said to be sophisticated today.

Ford Expands Factories in China 226

— (Huang Yingdai)

In the past two weeks, Mr. William C. Cowling, an important official of the American Ford Motor Company, came to China from the United States. He stayed in Shanghai for several days and recently departed from Shanghai to Manchuria and the northern provinces of China to conduct inspections. Mr. Cowling's sole purpose on this trip is to plan the expansion of Ford's business in China based on the conditions in various parts of China. In recent years, Ford has paid close attention to China's economic situation and conditions in various regions. The plan to expand its factories in China has long been in its heart.

During Mr. Cowling's stay in Shanghai, he was warmly welcomed by Chinese and Westerners and was very busy with social engagements. On the day of his departure to the north, Mr. Cowling told people that although he had not stayed in Shanghai for many days, he had a deep impression of Shanghai and the surrounding areas. He firmly believes that although China is in a state of chaos today, it will be the only automobile market in the Far East in the future. Because the provinces of China are actively developing, the sales of automobiles will have great development, which can be asserted. Mr. Cowling also shared Ford's economic observations with the people of Shanghai. Ford said, "Money and wealth cannot be regarded as the same thing. Wealth is derived from the people's experience, evolution, and efforts. As for money itself, it is completely powerless. Its existence depends on wealth. Without wealth, money is useless. Development and wealth should not be confused as one thing. Development is the flow of wealth. The two can be independent of each other and have no mutual relationship. Sometimes, the government of a country holds great wealth, while the people are quite poor. In other words, the people can also possess great resources, while the government is extremely poor. Therefore, wealth can sometimes make people rich and at the same time make them poor, possessing two opposite forces. The best power is the ability to build a solid foundation for general development." Ford's recent business plans are based on this principle. The salaries of employees and general business policies are also carried out accordingly.

Recently, various industries in the United States have experienced stagnation, and the wages of employees have also been reduced as a result. However, Ford is different. It has increased its spending in factories. Its vision is also conceivable. Ford believes that in order to seek the development of the business, one must first seek to increase the purchasing power of the society. In short, Ford's various business policies are not based on a compassionate and loving heart, but on a deep understanding of social economic principles. Therefore, it is still eager to expand the scope of its business. Recently, Ford has also paid extraordinary attention to road development, because the development of roads can increase the power of transportation. Therefore, Ford will personally attend the Road Research Conference held in the United States next year and express his opinions.

As for Mr. Cowling's visit to Shanghai, he was also quite satisfied in his heart. After an inspection, he already had a clue as to the location of the new factory. Ford had already mentioned in various American newspapers that it would establish a large-scale new factory in China, and Shanghai was considered the most suitable place to set up the factory. The problem of setting up a factory can be carried out according to its findings after Mr. Cowling returns to Shanghai in September.

Investigation

Overview of Public and Private Roads in Zhejiang Province 227

— Ping

Based on statistical reports from the Zhejiang Construction Department.

Explanation of the Process: The planning and construction of roads in Zhejiang began as early as 1920. In 1922, the Zhejiang Provincial Road Bureau was formally established, using tobacco taxes as funding for road construction. By 1926, the Xiaoshao section of the Zhejiang-Fujian Line was open to traffic. Completed sections included the Shengxin, Tianbai, Huangze, and Yongjia sections of the Zhejiang-Fujian Line. The Zhejiang-Anhui Secondary Line and Basic Line were under construction, and the Lancang section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Line had been surveyed. Roads contracted by merchants included the Hangyu, Yulin, Yuwu, Hangfu, Hanghai, Pinghu-Shuanglin, Ningchang, Shengxin-Shaocao, and Sheng lines. The outbreak of military conflicts affected all roads, leading to disrepair, vehicle damage, and a decline in business. Ongoing construction on various lines came to a standstill. In its initial stage, the Construction Department took over amidst widespread devastation and strived to restore order. It assigned specialists to investigate the condition of various roads as a basis for rectification and proposed converting the tobacco tax into a tobacco monopoly to increase revenue. When tobacco tax revenues were nationalized, construction funds suddenly became strained. However, road construction could not be delayed. Therefore, the department prioritized the Basic Ning-Feng Road and the Shaoxing connecting line, and began planning a province-wide road network. When the additional construction tax for each county was established, it was designated as road construction funding. The Provincial Road Bureau was reorganized into the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Bureau to formalize its name and issued highway bonds to meet urgent needs, which led to a gradual expansion of open roads and the completion of unfinished lines. Road surveying and construction began to progress actively. Merchants continued to contract roads, and the Ningyuan, Changyu, Shengchang, and Hangxian routes have all opened to traffic successively. Companies still in operation include the Quguang, Ningde, and Yuxiaoan companies. As of 1929, the total length of completed roads in the province was 784.74 kilometers. Publicly funded roads accounted for 438.64 kilometers, or 55.90%, while privately funded roads accounted for 346.10 kilometers, or 44.10%. Roads operating passenger vehicle services accounted for 555.29 kilometers, or 70.76%. According to historical road construction statistics, merchant-built roads were most developed in 1926, totaling 130.42 kilometers. Publicly funded road construction peaked in 1929, totaling 249.38 kilometers (excluding recovered merchant-built routes). Comparing road construction achievements over the past six years, 1929 was the most successful, with a total of 296.42 kilometers completed.

Provincial Road Network: The Construction Department, recognizing the somewhat rudimentary development of existing roads, pre-established a provincial road network to ensure uniform road administration and prevent future conflicts and duplication. It selected ten major trunk lines, totaling 2,795 kilometers, and forty branch lines, totaling 3,953 kilometers, for a grand total of 6,748 kilometers. This plan has been approved by the Provincial Government Committee at its 224th meeting. Once fully completed, a network of highways will extend throughout the province. The planned road network comprises over 6,700 kilometers, of which approximately one-tenth has already been constructed. Many other sections are underway or planned for completion within five years, and some are even planned for conversion into railways. Previously established and unfinished roads, as well as planned railway lines, along with the original road network, include six north-south trunk lines, three east-west trunk lines, and one coastal line, totaling 2,795 li. There are forty branch lines, totaling 3,953 li. The second north-south trunk line is now planned for conversion into the Xiaoshan-Jinhua railway. The Jinpu line, the second east-west trunk line, will be converted into the Lishui-Longquan railway. The Puan branch line and the Jianwei line will be converted into the Jiande-Weiping railway.

Highway Bureau Operations: The former road administration agency in this province was the Zhejiang Provincial Road Bureau, directly under the highest provincial administrative official. The bureau included an engineering department and administrative, business, and financial sections, each responsible for various tasks. During road construction, district engineering offices were established. Once sections were completed, management offices were established. The bureau chief and deputy bureau chief were appointed by the governor, while other staff were appointed by the bureau chief. With the establishment of the Construction Department, the Provincial Road Bureau was placed under its jurisdiction and underwent a reorganization. The bureau chief, deputy bureau chief, and chief engineer were all appointed by the provincial government. In April 1928, the Provincial Road Bureau was renamed the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Bureau, and its organizational regulations were slightly revised. Due to the urgency of construction on the Hangchang, Hangxian, Hangshi-Hangchang, Lancang, and Yongli lines, the provincial government issued organizational regulations for the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Bureau engineering offices to ensure compliance. Each district engineering office was staffed with an engineer to manage all engineering within the district. Districts were further divided into sections, each managed by an assistant engineer. In August 1928, the Gongsan section of the Hangshao Road, the basic line, was completed and opened to traffic. New projects on various roads were also actively underway. Due to the heavy workload, the Highway Bureau's organization had to be expanded. Therefore, in November 1928, the regulations for the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Bureau were submitted and approved by the provincial government. The differences from the original organization included the appointment of a chief engineer concurrently serving as the head of the engineering department, and a chief of machinery concurrently serving as the head of the vehicle department, both appointed by the provincial government. The original business section was merged into the vehicle department. The organization of the district engineering offices was also revised by the provincial government to allow for the rapid and separate construction of highways, resulting in the Zhejiang Highway Bureau District Engineering Office Organizational Regulations. Districts were divided into sections, each 50 to 60 li in length, and sections were further divided into subsections, each limited to 20 li. Each district was headed by a chief engineer. By the end of 1929, in addition to Gongsan, the Shaoxing connecting line, Ningfeng Road, Hangchang Road, and Hangping Road had been completed in succession, totaling 255.60 kilometers.

Privately Funded Roads: The earliest privately funded highway project in Zhejiang was the Hangyu Highway, proposed in 1922, followed by the Yulin, Yuwu, Hangfu (recovered by the province), Hanghai, Pinghu-Shuanglin, and Ningchang companies. The Shengxin section of the publicly funded Zhejiang-Fujian Line was also leased to a merchant-organized company for operation. Subsequently, the Shengsan, Jicaosheng, Ningyuan, Shengchang, Yuxiaoan, and Ningde roads were also initiated. To date, the Changyu, Hangping, and Qukang routes have also been organized. Therefore, there are a total of sixteen privately funded companies, with a total capital of 4,060,000 yuan in national currency. The largest capital was allocated to Jicaosheng, totaling 1,000,000 yuan in national currency, followed by Qukang at 600,000 yuan, Changyu at 400,000 yuan, Hanghai and Yulin both at 350,000 yuan, Shengchang at 320,000 yuan, and Hangyu and Yuwu both at 250,000 yuan. The trunk and branch lines of these privately funded highways total 96.31 kilometers, with 346.10 kilometers already constructed, 87.12 kilometers under construction, and 101.68 kilometers planned.

Number of Vehicles: The Hangshao Road has the most vehicles. The Xiaoshao Road has 65 vehicles, the Gongsan Road has 23 vehicles, the Hangyu Road has 31 vehicles, the Hangchang Road has 29 vehicles, the Hanghai Road has 28 vehicles, and the Shaocaosheng Road has 27 vehicles. For passenger vehicles, excluding the Gongsan section of the Hangshao Road, which also operates on city streets and thus has a particularly high number, the Hangshao Road and Xiaoshao Road have the highest number, with 94.5 vehicles, followed by the Hangyu Road with 63.6 vehicles, and the Shaocaosheng Road with 54.6 vehicles. The Ningyuan Road has the lowest number with 9 vehicles, and the Changyu Road with 7.2 vehicles. For small chartered cars, the Shaocaosheng Road has the highest number with 24.5 vehicles, followed by the Hangshao Road and Hangyu Road with 23.1 vehicles each, the Shengchang Road with 17 vehicles, the Hangxi Road with 16.1 vehicles, and Yuwu with 14.4 vehicles. By category, there are 293 vehicles for business purposes and 32 vehicles for operational and official purposes. Among the vehicles for business purposes, passenger vehicles are the most numerous, with 211 ordinary passenger vehicles and 71 small chartered cars, totaling 282 vehicles. This indicates that all highways in the province are primarily focused on passenger transport, with only the Changyu and Pinghu-Shuanglin roads generating significant revenue.

Construction of Various Roads: Highway construction should primarily meet the needs of modern transportation. Engineering facilities must align with broad, flat, and straight conditions to ensure driving safety, passenger trust, and business development. If the roadbed is narrow, the slope is steep, the curvature is sharp, and the road surface is uneven, vehicles will experience bumps and vibrations, causing discomfort to passengers. Excessive shaking can damage parts, and vehicles may even overturn, endangering passengers' lives. Zhejiang Province follows the requirements of the Ministry of Railways for highway engineering and also has its own regulations. The minimum radius of curves is 16 meters, and the maximum slope is set at 4%. In unavoidable circumstances, it can be increased to 8%. The narrowest road surface width is 4.5 meters, and the widest is 7 meters.

Circus Using General Motors Truck 228

Qiong Bo, an important member of a major American circus, relies on General Motors trucks to transport equipment between states for performances. General Motors trucks are produced by the American General Motors Manufacturing Plant. The truck bodies are exceptionally large, with sufficient load capacity, comfortable stability, and speed, while also being economical. General Motors trucks are used in various countries around the world, and are now trusted in various regions of China. They are indeed unique trucks.

The most common width is 5 to 6 meters. The road surfaces used include crushed stone roads, cinder roads, snail shell roads, cobblestone roads, sand-earth roads, paved streets, and concrete roads.

News

Anhui Highway Department Adds Vehicles 229

— Heping

The Anhui Highway Department is directly under the Construction Department, with the department director, Li Fanyi, concurrently serving as the head of the department. Currently, three sections of highways in the province are open to traffic: the Anqian Road from Anqing to Qianshan, totaling 92 kilometers; the Jingwu Road from Wuhu to Dangtu, totaling 28 kilometers; and the Hechao Road from Hefei to Chaoxian, totaling 72 kilometers. There are a total of 42 long-distance buses for passenger and freight transport. From September of last year to June of this year, the business revenue and expenditures could not offset each other due to the initial startup period, resulting in a total loss of over 33,000 yuan. Starting in July of this year, efforts have been made to rectify the situation by increasing revenue and reducing expenditures. Despite the impact of rising gasoline prices, there is still a monthly surplus, and the future is very optimistic. However, at the beginning of July, the Transportation Department of the General Headquarters issued an order to requisition 16 trucks for a military-use heavy vehicle committee for the war zone, which has caused transportation difficulties. Now that the autumn harvest is plentiful, and the transport of rice and grains relies on automobiles, Director Li has decided to purchase an additional ten vehicles. Representatives from the Shanghai Ford Motor Company, Yu Tengfang and Li Jiashi, as well as the deputy manager of General Motors, Tao Fu, and Yan Jiqing, have successively arrived in Anhui to discuss the matter. It is expected that a decision will be made soon, and the new vehicles will be delivered.
